Eight Scenarios of Recitation in Nafl Prayer and Their Rulings
Analysis of eight recitation scenarios in nafl prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the number of rak'ahs to make up (qada) in each of the eight scenarios of recitation in a four-rak'ah nafl prayer, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Omitting recitation in nafl prayer requires compensation (qada) per pair; disputes arise on whether corruption spreads.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira presents a detailed analysis of eight specific cases of recitation in a four-rak'ah nafl prayer. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the first pair (shaf' awwal) and second pair (shaf' thani) of rak'ahs. The ruling hinges on whether the tahrima remains valid, and whether the worshipper sits between the pairs. The passage enumerates four agreed cases and four disputed ones among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Understand the prayer structure
A four-rak'ah nafl prayer consists of two pairs (shaf'): the first two rak'ahs (shaf' awwal) and the last two (shaf' thani). A sitting (tashahhud) between the pairs is typical.
If the sitting is omitted, the prayer's structure changes and corruption may spread.
2
Apply the core principle
The opening takbir (tahrima) remains valid even if recitation is omitted in some rak'ahs. Thus the prayer continues, but compensation (qada) is required for the pair where recitation was omitted.
Compensation means repeating those rak'ahs after the prayer, but the prayer itself is not invalidated.
3
Identify the four agreed-upon scenarios
The passage states four cases where all three imams agree that only the second pair (two rak'ahs) must be made up: (1) recited in first two only, (2) recited in first two and one of last two, (3) recited in last two only, (4) recited in one of first two and last two.
In these cases, the first pair is valid because recitation occurred in at least one rak'ah.
4
Analyze the four disputed scenarios
In four cases, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ: (a) recited in only one of the first two: Abu Yusuf says four, others say two. (b) recited in only one of the last two: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say four, Muhammad says two. (c) recited in one of first two and one of last two: Abu Yusuf says four, Muhammad says two. (d) recited in one of first two (or none): Abu Yusuf says four, others say two.
The dispute centers on whether the corruption spreads from an invalid pair to a valid one, especially when there is no sitting between pairs.
5
Apply the sitting rule
If the worshipper does not sit between the pairs, then corruption from an invalid second pair spreads to the first, requiring all four rak'ahs to be made up. This is mentioned in al-Nihaya.
This ruling applies only if recitation was omitted in the second pair and no sitting occurred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما أبو يوسف فيقول : فسد الشفع الأول والثاني يلزمه بمجرد القيام، وعند أبي حنيفة : وجد منه ركعة بقراءة، ثم فسدت بعد. ه والخامسة: إذا قرأ في الأوليين، وإحدى الأُخريين: لزمه قضاء الأخريين، بالإجماع؛ لأن الشفع الأول قد صح، والثاني يلزمه بمجرد القيام. ٦- والسادسة: إذا قرأ في الأخريين، وإحدى الأوليين: فالأوليان فسدتا، ويلزمه قضاؤهما بالإجماع، والأخريان صلاة عندهما، خلافاً لمحمد. والسابعة : إذا قرأ في إحدى الأوليين، لا غير: فعليه قضاء ركعتين عندهما، وقال أبو يوسف: أربع. والثامنة : إذا قرأ في إحدى الأخريين، لا غير: فعليه قضاء أربع عندهما، وقال محمد ركعتين. ولو لم يقرأ في الأوليين، وقرأ في الأخريين، ونوى به قضاء الأوليين: لا يكون قضاء، بالإجماع؛ لأنها صلاة واحدة عقدت بتحريمة واحدة، فلا يكون بعضها قضاء، وبعضها أداء. قال في النهاية»: إذا قرأ في الأوليين، لا غير فعليه قضاء الأخريين، بالإجماع؛ لأن التحريمة لم تبطل فصح الشروع في الشفع الثاني، ثم فساده بترك القراءة: لا يُفسد الشفعَ الأول. قال: وهذا إذا قعد بينهما، أما إذا لم يقعد: فعليه قضاء أربع؛ لأن الفساد في الثاني يسري إلى الأول إذا لم يقعد. فبان لك من هذه الثمان المسائل: أن أربعاً منها مجمع عليها، وهن: إذا قرأ في الأوليين لا غير، أو في الأوليين وإحدى الأُخريين، أو في الأخريين لا غير، أو في إحدى الأوليين والأخريين، ففي هذه الأربع يقضي ركعتين، إجماعاً. وأربع مختلف فيها : إذا قرأ في إحدى الأخريين، لا غير، أو في إحدى الأوليين وإحدى الأخريين : يقضي أربعاً عندهما، وعند محمد ركعتين. ولو قرأ في إحدى الأوليين، أو لم يقرأ في الكل: يقضي ركعتين عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف أربعاً.
As for Abu Yusuf, he says: the first pair [of rak'ahs] becomes invalid, and the second pair becomes obligatory upon him by the mere standing. According to Abu Hanifa: he performed one rak'ah with recitation, then it became invalid afterwards. Fifth: If he recited in the first two and one of the last two, then he must make up the last two by consensus, because the first pair is valid, and the second pair becomes obligatory upon him by the mere standing. Sixth: If he recited in the last two and one of the first two, then the first two became invalid, and he must make them up by consensus, and the last two are valid according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), contrary to Muhammad. Seventh: If he recited in only one of the first two, then he must make up two rak'ahs according to them, and Abu Yusuf said: four. Eighth: If he recited in only one of the last two, then he must make up four according to them, and Muhammad said: two rak'ahs. And if he did not recite in the first two and recited in the last two, intending thereby to make up the first two, it does not count as make-up by consensus, because it is one prayer contracted with one takbir, so part of it cannot be make-up and part ad hoc. He said in al-Nihaya: If he recited in the first two only, he must make up the last two by consensus, because the opening takbir did not become invalid, so the commencement of the second pair was sound, then its corruption due to leaving recitation does not corrupt the first pair. He said: This is if he sat between them; but if he did not sit, then he must make up four, because the corruption in the second spreads to the first if he did not sit. So it becomes clear to you from these eight issues: that four of them are agreed upon, and they are: if he recited in the first two only, or in the first two and one of the last two, or in the last two only, or in one of the first two and the last two, then in these four he makes up two rak'ahs by consensus. And four are disputed: if he recited in one of the last two only, or in one of the first two and one of the last two, he makes up four according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Muhammad two rak'ahs. And if he recited in one of the first two, or did not recite at all, he makes up two rak'ahs according to them, and according to Abu Yusuf four.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute analyzing eight specific scenarios of recitation in a four-rak'ah nafl prayer. It details the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding qada (making up) when recitation is omitted in certain rak'ahs. The text begins with a statement from Abu Yusuf about the first pair (shaf' al-awwal) and second pair (shaf' al-thani) becoming invalid or obligatory. Then it enumerates six specific cases (fifth through eighth, plus two additional ones). The summary at the end classifies four scenarios as agreed upon (mujma' 'alayha) and four as disputed (mukhtalif fiha). Note that the term 'first pair' refers to the first two rak'ahs, and 'second pair' to the last two. The ruling hinges on whether the initial takbir (tahrima) remains valid. If the tahrima is valid, the prayer continues; omission of recitation in a rak'ah does not invalidate the entire prayer but requires compensation. The dispute among the Hanafi imams centers on whether the corruption spreads from one pair to the other, especially when the worshipper does not sit between the pairs (i.e., fails to separate them with a sitting).

Key Terms
الشفع (al-shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; in a four-rak'ah nafl prayer, the first two rak'ahs and the last two rak'ahs are each considered a shaf'.
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed or invalidated rak'ah; here it refers to repeating the rak'ahs that were performed incorrectly due to omission of recitation.
تحريمة (tahrima): The opening takbir which commences the prayer; its validity is crucial for the prayer's continuity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which of the following scenarios do all three imams agree that only two rak'ahs must be made up?
A) Recited in one of the first two only
B) Recited in one of the last two only
C) Recited in the first two and one of the last two
D) Recited in one of the first two and one of the last two

Key Takeaway
In a four-rak'ah nafl prayer, omission of recitation necessitates qada of the affected pair, but the exact number ranges from two to four depending on the scenario and the imam's view.

Voluntary Prayer While Seated: Ruling and Proof
Ruling statement with hadith proof and an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing nafl prayer while seated, cite the hadith proof, and explain the objection raised regarding its dalal.

Core Idea
The prayer of one seated is half the reward of one standing – this hadith proves the permissibility of sitting nafl prayer even for one able to stand.

The Hanafi school permits performing voluntary prayer (nafl) while sitting, even for those who are physically able to stand. This ruling is based on a well-known hadith that compares the reward of sitting versus standing. However, the ruling is not free from scholarly discussion. In this lesson we will examine the proof structure and the objection that has been raised, which challenges the use of the hadith for this specific ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the matn: it states that one may pray nafl while sitting even if able to stand. This is the Hanafi position.
The ruling is unconditional—no excuse required.
2
Locate the hadith proof
The commentary cites the hadith: 'The prayer of the seated is half of the prayer of the standing.' Note that the commentator adds 'meaning in terms of reward'.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari (1115).
3
Understand what the hadith indicates
The hadith compares reward, not validity. It shows that sitting prayer is valid but less rewarded. This supports permissibility.
The key phrase is 'على النصف' (half).
4
Recognize the objection raised
The text raises an objection: the hadith does not specify whether it applies to obligatory or voluntary prayers, nor to states of excuse. So how does it prove the claimed ruling?
The objection is left unanswered in this passage; a response follows in later text.
5
Reflect on the Hanafi reasoning despite the objection
Even though the hadith is general, the Hanafi school applies it to nafl because the reward comparison is unconditional. For fard, standing is a pillar, so the hadith cannot override that obligation.
The ruling is considered established in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصلي النافلة قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام . قوله: (ويصلي النافلة قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام). لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «صلاةُ القاعد على النصف من صلاة القائم»، أي في حق الأجر. فإن قيل: هذا الحديث لم يتعرض لصلاة الفرض، ولا لصلاة التطوع، ولا لحالة العذر، ولا لحالة غير العذر، فما وجه الاحتجاج به على ما ادعيتموه، من جواز صلاة النافلة قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام؟ (١) بلفظ قريب في صحيح البخاري (١١١٥).
And he prays the voluntary prayer sitting while being able to stand. His statement: 'And he prays the voluntary prayer sitting while being able to stand.' Because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'The prayer of the seated person is half of the prayer of the standing person,' meaning in terms of reward. If it is said: This hadith does not address obligatory prayer, nor voluntary prayer, nor the state of excuse, nor the state of no excuse, so what is the basis of using it as evidence for what you claim, that it is permissible to pray voluntary prayer sitting while being able to stand? (1) With a close wording in Sahih al-Bukhari (1115).
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and proof for performing nafl prayer while seated despite being able to stand. The matn simply states the ruling. The commentary then cites the hadith 'صلاة القاعد على النصف من صلاة القائم' (The prayer of one sitting is half the prayer of one standing). The commentator explains that this refers to reward (ajr). The objection raised is that the hadith does not specify whether it applies to obligatory or voluntary prayers, nor to situations of excuse or otherwise. The objection points out that the hadith cannot be used to deduce permissibility for one who is able to stand unless it is explicitly about voluntary prayers. The passage ends with the objection without answer, suggesting the answer may follow in subsequent text.

Key Terms
النافلة (al-nafila): Voluntary, supererogatory prayer.
القاعد (al-qa'id): One who prays sitting; the hadith refers to the reward comparison.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, what is the reward of a voluntary prayer performed while sitting compared to standing?
A) Full reward
B) Half reward
C) Quarter reward
D) No reward

Key Takeaway
It is permissible to perform nafl prayer while seated even without excuse, but the reward is half that of standing.

Rulings on Nafl Prayer: Sitting and Recitation Omission
Expands Quduri's matn on nafl prayer rulings and Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying nafl while sitting, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on changing posture, and apply the consensus and dispute patterns for recitation omission in four-rak'ah nafl.

Core Idea
Nafl prayer is built on leniency: sitting without excuse is permissible but with half reward, but starting standing then sitting is disputed.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayirah unpacks two key rulings related to voluntary (nafl) prayers: the consequences of omitting recitation in certain rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah nafl, and the permissibility of praying nafl while sitting. The text first clarifies a consensus-versus-dispute map for eight recitation scenarios, then tackles the ruling on sitting in nafl, including an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether one may sit after having started standing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main issues
The passage covers two distinct topics: (1) rulings on recitation omission in a four-rak'ah nafl, and (2) permissibility of praying nafl while sitting. Recognise that the commentary bridges these by first discussing the 'sitting between rak'ahs' connection.
2
Map the eight recitation scenarios
The text lists eight scenarios for recitation in a four-rak'ah nafl. Four are agreed upon (consensus) requiring qada' of two rak'ahs; four are disputed with differences among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. Trace each scenario and note which scholars hold which view.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi; note that 'عندهما' sometimes means Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but at times the text distinguishes individual positions.
3
Analyse the proof for sitting in nafl
The passage cites the hadith 'prayer of the sitting is half the prayer of the standing' for reward. It then addresses a potential objection: the hadith does not specify nafl. The response uses consensus on fard and sick person's prayer to isolate the category of healthy person's nafl sitting.
This is an example of takhsis al-amm (specifying a general text) through contextual evidence.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting after standing
If one starts a nafl prayer standing then sits without excuse, Abu Hanifa permits it (istihsan), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require an excuse and analogise to fard (qiyas). Understand the methodological difference: istihsan vs. qiyas.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's, based on the principle that nafl is founded on ease.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical difference: if someone sits without excuse, according to Abu Hanifa the prayer is valid with half reward; according to the Sahibayn it is invalid and must be repeated. This affects everyday practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل
ويصلي النافلة قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام .
قال: وهذا إذا قعد بينهما، أما إذا لم يقعد: فعليه قضاء أربع؛ لأن الفساد في الثاني يسري إلى الأول إذا لم يقعد.
فبان لك من هذه الثمان المسائل:
أن أربعاً منها مجمع عليها، وهن:
إذا قرأ في الأوليين لا غير، أو في الأوليين وإحدى الأُخريين، أو في الأخريين لا غير، أو في إحدى الأوليين والأخريين، ففي هذه الأربع يقضي ركعتين، إجماعاً.
وأربع مختلف فيها : إذا قرأ في إحدى الأخريين، لا غير، أو في إحدى الأوليين وإحدى الأخريين : يقضي أربعاً عندهما، وعند محمد ركعتين. ولو قرأ في إحدى الأوليين، أو لم يقرأ في الكل: يقضي ركعتين عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف أربعاً.
* قوله: (ويصلي النافلة قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام). لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «صلاةُ القاعد على النصف من صلاة القائم»، أي في حق الأجر.
فإن قيل: هذا الحديث لم يتعرض لصلاة الفرض، ولا لصلاة التطوع، ولا لحالة العذر، ولا لحالة غير العذر، فما وجه الاحتجاج به على ما ادعيتموه، من جواز صلاة النافلة قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام؟
(۱) بلفظ قريب في صحيح البخاري (١١١٥).
ثم قعد من غير عُذر : جاز عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : لا يجوز إلا من عذر .
قيل : الإجماع منعقد على أن صلاة الفرض قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام: لا تجوز.
وكذا الإجماع منعقد على أن صلاة المريض العاجز عن القيام قاعداً: مساوية لصلاة القائم في الفضيلة والأجر.
فلم يبق حينئذ إلا صلاة التطوع قاعداً بدون العذر: فهو على نصف الأجر من صلاة القائم. وإنما جازت النافلة قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام؛ لأن الصلاة خير موضوع، وربما يشق عليه القيام فجاز له تركه؛ كي لا ينقطع عن هذا الخير الموضوع.
وقيد بالنافلة : احترازاً عن الفرض، والوتر.
قال في «الهداية»(۱) : والسنن الرواتب : نوافل، يعني يجوز أن يصليها قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام
واختلفوا في كيفية القعود : قيل : كيف يشاء والمختار: أنه يقعد كما يقعد في التشهد.
قَعَدَ من غير عذر: جاز عند أبي حنيفة، هذا استحسان، وعندهما لا يجوز إلا من عذر)، وهو القياس؛
Chapter of voluntary prayers. He prays the voluntary prayer sitting despite ability to stand. He said: This is if he sits between them; but if he does not sit, then upon him is to make up four rak'ahs, because the corruption in the second spreads to the first if he does not sit. So it becomes clear from these eight issues: That four of them are unanimous upon: when he recites in the first two only, or in the first two and one of the last two, or in the last two only, or in one of the first two and the last two – in these four he makes up two rak'ahs by consensus. And four are disputed: if he recites in one of the last two only, or in one of the first two and one of the last two: he makes up four according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Muhammad two rak'ahs. And if he recites in one of the first two, or does not recite at all: he makes up two rak'ahs according to them, and according to Abu Yusuf four. * His statement: (And he prays the voluntary prayer sitting despite ability to stand). Due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'The prayer of the one sitting is half the prayer of the one standing,' i.e., regarding reward. For it is said: This hadith does not address obligatory prayer, nor voluntary prayer, nor the state of excuse, nor the state of no excuse; so what is the basis for arguing with it for what you claim, of permissibility of voluntary prayer while sitting despite ability to stand? Then he sits without excuse: it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, and the two said: not permissible except with an excuse. It is said: Consensus is established that obligatory prayer while sitting despite ability to stand is not permissible. Likewise, consensus is established that the prayer of the sick unable to stand while sitting is equal to the prayer of the standing in virtue and reward. So then nothing remains except voluntary prayer sitting without excuse: it is half the reward of the standing prayer. And voluntary prayer is permissible sitting despite ability to stand because prayer is a good thing, and perhaps standing may be difficult for him, so it is permissible for him to leave it so that he is not cut off from this good thing. And it is restricted to voluntary prayer to exclude obligatory and witr. He said in al-Hidayah: The regular sunnahs are voluntary, meaning it is permissible to pray them sitting despite ability to stand. And they differed regarding the manner of sitting: it is said: however he wishes, and the preferred view is that he sits as he sits in the tashahhud. He sat without excuse: it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, this is istihsan; and according to the two it is not permissible except with an excuse, and that is qiyas.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayirah, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, covers two main issues: (1) the consequences of omitting recitation in certain rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah nafl prayer, and (2) the ruling on praying nafl while sitting, including the dispute about starting standing then sitting without excuse.

The commentator first explains a prior statement about sitting between rak'ahs. He clarifies that if one sits between the second and third rak'ah (the default in a four-rak'ah nafl), then omitting recitation in certain patterns only requires making up two rak'ahs. But if one does not sit (i.e., prays continuously without the tashahhud between), then corruption spreads, requiring qada of four rak'ahs. He then summarizes eight scenarios: four where there is consensus that only two rak'ahs are made up (recitation in first two only; first two and one of last two; last two only; one of first two and last two). The other four are disputed: in two cases (recitation in one of last two only; one of first two and one of last two) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require four rak'ahs, but Muhammad says two. In the remaining two (recitation in one of first two only; no recitation at all) Abu Yusuf requires four while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say two. Note the asymmetry: the positions of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) are not always identical here; the text distinguishes 'عندهما' (according to the two) vs. 'عند أبي يوسف' and 'عند محمد'.

The second part addresses the matn's ruling: 'He prays voluntary prayer sitting despite ability to stand.' The commentator provides the hadith: 'The prayer of the one sitting is half the prayer of the one standing' in terms of reward. He then anticipates a challenge: the hadith is general and does not specify voluntary prayer or the state of having no excuse. His response: Since there is consensus that obligatory prayer while sitting with ability to stand is invalid, and that the sick person sitting gets full reward, the only remaining category is voluntary prayer by a healthy person sitting without excuse, and the hadith confirms it is permissible with half reward. The rationale is that prayer is a good act, and allowing sitting prevents the person from abandoning it entirely due to difficulty.

He then restricts the ruling to nafl, excluding fard and witr. Referring to al-Hidayah, he notes that the regular sunnahs (rawatib) are included in nafl. On the manner of sitting, the preferred view is to sit like in tashahhud, though some say any sitting is fine.

Finally, the passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: If one starts a nafl prayer standing and then sits without excuse, Abu Hanifa allows it based on istihsan (juristic preference), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disallow it except with an excuse, analogizing (qiyas) to obligatory prayer where such an act would invalidate the prayer. The commentator notes that the view of Abu Hanifa is the relied-upon position in the school.

Key Terms
النافلة (al-nāfilah): Voluntary/optional prayer beyond the obligatory ones.
القضاء (al-qaḍāʾ): Making up a prayer that was not performed correctly; here it refers to repeating rak'ahs within the same prayer.
الاستحسان (al-istiḥsān): Juristic preference, a method of legal reasoning that deems something good and sets aside qiyas in favor of leniency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if someone begins a nafl prayer standing and then sits down without an excuse, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid with half the reward.
C) The prayer is valid only if the person intended to sit from the beginning.
D) The prayer becomes obligatory to complete sitting.

Key Takeaway
In nafl prayer, leniency prevails: sitting without excuse is valid but with half reward, and the Hanafi school follows Abu Hanifa's view that starting standing then sitting is permissible.

Ruling on Sitting in Voluntary Prayer After Starting Standing
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting without excuse in supererogatory prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on sitting without excuse in voluntary prayer and explain the distinction between nathr and shuru' that supports the Hanafi tarjih.

Core Idea
Sitting without excuse in voluntary prayer is permissible per Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn disagree based on qiyas with a vow.

This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayirah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Sahibayn). The issue is whether a person who starts a voluntary (nafl) prayer standing may sit down without a valid excuse. Imam Abu Hanifa permits it based on istihsan (juristic preference), while the Sahibayn require an excuse based on qiyas (analogy) with a vow (nathr). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to see how different usul principles—istihsan vs. qiyas—yield different rulings within the same madhhab, and how the later school settled on Abu Hanifa's view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what Imam Abu Hanifa rules regarding sitting without excuse in a voluntary prayer after starting standing.
Abu Hanifa says it is permissible (ja'iz).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Determine which scholars disagree and what they require.
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) require an excuse.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the qiyas argument of the Sahibayn: starting an act creates a binding commitment like a vow.
They analogize 'shuru'' to 'nathr'.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine Abu Hanifa's rebuttal using istihsan and the distinction that a vow is explicit while starting is not.
He cites examples from fasting and pilgrimage to show the difference.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence of the difference: which position is followed in fatwa?
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view; one may sit without excuse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل
وإن افتتحها قائماً، ثم قعد من غير عذر : جاز عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : لا يجوز إلا من عذر .
قيل : الإجماع منعقد على أن صلاة الفرض قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام: لا تجوز.
وكذا الإجماع منعقد على أن صلاة المريض العاجز عن القيام قاعداً: مساوية لصلاة القائم في الفضيلة والأجر.
فلم يبق حينئذ إلا صلاة التطوع قاعداً بدون العذر: فهو على نصف الأجر من صلاة القائم. وإنما جازت النافلة قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام؛ لأن الصلاة خير موضوع، وربما يشق عليه القيام فجاز له تركه؛ كي لا ينقطع عن هذا الخير الموضوع.
وقيد بالنافلة : احترازاً عن الفرض، والوتر.
قال في «الهداية» : والسنن الرواتب : نوافل، يعني يجوز أن يصليها قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام
واختلفوا في كيفية القعود : قيل : كيف يشاء والمختار: أنه يقعد كما يقعد في التشهد.
قعد من غير عذر: جاز عند أبي حنيفة، هذا استحسان، وعندهما لا يجوز إلا من عذر، وهو القياس؛ لأن الشروع معتبر بالنذر ، من حيث إن كل واحد منهما ملزم. ثم من نذر أن يصلي ركعتين قائماً : لم يجز له أن يقعد فيهما من غير عذر، فكذا إذا شرع قائماً: لم يجز له أن يقعد فيهما من غير عذر. وله: أنه إذا افتتح التطوع قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام: جاز، فالبقاء أولى، بخلاف النذر : فإنه التزمه نصاً، حتى لو لم ينص على القيام: لا يلزمه القيام عند بعض المشايخ على ما نبين إن شاء الله تعالى.
والدليل على التفرقة بين الشروع والنذر : أنه لو نذر أن يصوم متتابعاً، فصام البعض، ومرض، وأفطر يلزمه الاستئناف، وفي الشروع: لا يلزمه الاستئناف.
وكذا إذا نذر أن يحج ماشياً لزمه ماشياً، ولو شرع فيه ماشياً: لم يلزمه المشي، كذا هنا.
فإن قيل : إذا افتتحها قائماً هل له أن يقعد عند أبي حنيفة في الركعة الأولى بعد شروعه قائماً، كما له أن يقعد في الثانية؟
قيل : نعم ؛ لأن إطلاق وضعه يدل على الجواز.
ولو نذر صلاةً، ولم يقل: قائماً أو قاعداً:
قال بعضهم: هو بالخيار بين القعود والقيام، وقال بعضهم: يلزمه قائماً؛ لأن إيجاب العبد معتبر بإيجاب الله تعالى وكل ما أوجبه الله تعالى من الصلوات: أوجبه قائماً.
Chapter of Voluntary Prayers. If he begins it standing, then sits without an excuse: it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, and the two say: it is not permissible except with an excuse. It is said: consensus is established that the obligatory prayer sitting while able to stand is not valid. Likewise consensus is established that the prayer of a sick person unable to stand while sitting is equal in virtue and reward to the prayer of one standing. So nothing remains then except the supererogatory prayer sitting without excuse: it is on half the reward of the standing prayer. And the supererogatory prayer sitting while able to stand is only permissible because prayer is a good subject (khayr mawdu‘), and perhaps standing may be arduous for him, so he is allowed to leave it so that he is not cut off from this good subject. It is restricted to supererogatory prayers to exclude the obligatory and witr. He said in al-Hidayah: The regular sunnahs are supererogatory prayers, meaning it is permissible to perform them sitting while able to stand. And they differed about the manner of sitting: it is said: however he wishes; and the chosen view is that he sits as he sits in the tashahhud. ... (the passage continues)
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (al-Sahibayn), regarding the ruling on sitting in a voluntary (nafl) prayer after having started it standing, without a valid excuse. Abu Hanifa holds that it is permissible (ja'iz) based on istihsan (juristic preference). His reasoning is that since it is permissible to begin a voluntary prayer sitting even when one can stand, then remaining sitting (after having started standing) is a fortiori permissible. The Sahibayn hold that it is not permissible without an excuse, based on qiyas (analogy) with a vow (nathr). They argue that starting an act of worship creates a binding commitment similar to a vow; just as one who vows to pray two rak'ahs standing cannot sit without excuse, so too one who starts praying standing cannot sit. The text then provides a distinction: in a vow, the commitment is explicit and textual, whereas in starting the prayer, it is not. This distinction is supported by examples from fasting and pilgrimage. The passage also clarifies that the ruling applies only to voluntary prayers (nawafil), not to obligatory prayers or witr. It further includes the preferred manner of sitting, which is like the tashahhud position. Finally, it addresses the question of whether one may sit in the first rak'ah after starting standing, and Abu Hanifa's answer is yes, as the general permission indicates. A subsidiary issue about vowing a prayer without specifying standing or sitting is also discussed, with two opinions: one gives a choice, the other mandates standing by analogy to Allah's obligations.

Key Terms
النافلة (al-nāfilah): Supererogatory or voluntary prayer beyond the obligatory and sunnah mu'akkadah.
الاستحسان (al-istihsān): Juristic preference that allows a departure from strict analogy (qiyas) for a stronger reason, such as ease or established practice.
النذر (al-nadhr): A vow by which a person obligates themselves to perform an act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person begins a voluntary prayer standing, can he sit without an excuse?
A) No, it is not permissible without an excuse.
B) Yes, it is permissible even without an excuse.
C) It is only permissible if he sits in the first rak'ah.
D) It is permissible only if he intended to sit from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon view is that one may sit in a voluntary prayer after starting standing without an excuse, based on istihsan overriding the Sahibayn's qiyas.

The Legal Distinction Between Shuru' (Commencement) and Nadhr (Vow) in Supererogatory Prayers
Explains intra-Hanafi distinction between shuru' and nadhr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa distinguishes between commencing a nafl prayer and making a vow, and apply the rule to determine whether sitting is permitted in the first rak'ah of a nafl prayer started standing.

Core Idea
Starting a supererogatory prayer does not bind you like a vow — the default in nafl is flexibility.

This lesson dives into an intra-Hanafi debate: does commencing a nafl prayer standing impose an obligation to remain standing, similar to a vow? The text from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira presents the proof that Abu Hanifa distinguishes the two. Understanding this nuance is key to correctly applying the ruling on voluntary prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is supererogatory prayer (nafl). The dispute: if one starts it standing, is sitting permissible without excuse? Some scholars equate commencing a nafl (shuru') with a vow (nadhr), making standing obligatory. Abu Hanifa rejects this.
Note the key terms: shuru' and nadhr.
2
Contrast the two positions
Opposing view: shuru' and nadhr are both binding (mulzim), so if a vow to pray standing requires standing, then starting a nafl standing requires standing. Abu Hanifa: they are different because nafl is inherently flexible.
The opposing view is attributed to some Hanafi scholars, possibly Sahibayn.
3
Trace the Hanafi proof
Abu Hanifa's evidence: (1) One may start a nafl prayer sitting even if able to stand, so remaining in the starting posture is more appropriate. (2) Analogies from fasting and Hajj: breaking a vow requires restart, but discontinuing a voluntary act does not. (3) The unrestricted nature (itlaq al-wad') of the nafl indicates permissibility of sitting.
These are qiyas jali (clear analogy) arguments.
4
Apply the ruling
Thus, according to Abu Hanifa, one may sit in any rak'ah (first or second) of a nafl prayer started standing. The mufta bihi position is this flexibility.
The text explicitly answers 'yes' to the question about sitting in the first rak'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل
لأن الشروع معتبر بالنذر ، من حيث إن كل واحد منهما ملزم. ثم من نذر أن يصلي ركعتين قائماً : لم يجز له أن يقعد فيهما من غير عذر، فكذا إذا شرع قائماً: لم يجز له أن يقعد فيهما من غير عذر. وله: أنه إذا افتتح التطوع قاعداً . مع القدرة على القيام: جاز، فالبقاء أولى، بخلاف النذر : فإنه التزمه نصاً، حتى لو لم ينص على القيام: لا يلزمه القيام عند بعض المشايخ على ما نبين إن شاء الله تعالى.
والدليل على التفرقة بين الشروع والنذر : أنه لو نذر أن يصوم متتابعاً، فصام البعض، ومرض، وأفطر يلزمه الاستئناف، وفي الشروع: لا يلزمه الاستئناف.
:
وكذا إذا نذر أن يحج ماشياً لزمه ماشياً، ولو شرع فيه ماشياً: لم يلزمه المشي، كذا هنا.
فإن قيل : إذا افتتحها قائماً هل له أن يقعد عند أبي حنيفة في الركعة الأولى بعد شروعه قائماً، كما له أن يقعد في الثانية؟
قيل : نعم ؛ لأن إطلاق وضعه يدل على الجواز.
ولو نذر صلاةً، ولم يقل: قائماً أو قاعداً:
قال بعضهم: هو بالخيار بين القعود والقيام، وقال بعضهم: يلزمه قائماً؛ لأن إيجاب العبد معتبر بإيجاب الله تعالى وكل ما أوجبه الله تعالى من الصلوات: أوجبه قائماً.
Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers. Because commencement is considered like a vow, in that each one is binding. Then, whoever vows to pray two rak'ahs standing: it is not permissible for him to sit in them without an excuse; likewise, if he commences standing: it is not permissible for him to sit in them without an excuse. And for him (Abu Hanifa): if he begins a supererogatory prayer sitting, despite ability to stand: it is permissible, so remaining (in the same posture) is more appropriate, unlike the vow: for he obligated himself explicitly, such that if he did not specify standing: standing is not obligatory upon him according to some mashayikh, as we will explain if Allah wills. And the evidence for the distinction between commencement and a vow is: if he vowed to fast consecutively, then fasted some, then became ill and broke his fast, he must start over; but in commencement, he does not have to start over. Likewise, if he vowed to perform Hajj walking, he must do so walking; but if he commenced it walking, walking is not obligatory upon him; similarly here. If it is said: If he begins it standing, does he have the right to sit according to Abu Hanifa in the first rak'ah after commencing standing, just as he has the right to sit in the second? It is said: Yes; because the unrestricted nature of his act indicates permissibility. And if he vows a prayer and does not say 'standing' or 'sitting': Some said: he has the choice between sitting and standing; and some said: he must pray standing; because the obligation of the servant is considered by the obligation of Allah Almighty, and every prayer that Allah Almighty has made obligatory He made it standing.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar addresses the ruling of standing and sitting in supererogatory (nafl) prayers. The discussion begins by comparing the commencement of a nafl act (shuru') to a vow (nadh): some scholars equate them, arguing that both are binding. Therefore, if one vows to pray two rak'ahs standing, he cannot sit without excuse; similarly, if he starts a nafl prayer standing, he cannot sit. However, the author presents the view of Abu Hanifa (identified by 'lahu') who distinguishes: if one starts nafl sitting despite being able to stand, it is permissible; so remaining in the initial posture is more appropriate, unlike a vow where the obligation is explicit. The evidence for the distinction is given through examples: if one vows to fast consecutively and breaks it due to illness, he must start over; but in the case of starting a voluntary fast, restart is not required. Similarly, vowing to walk in Hajj obligates walking, but starting a voluntary walking does not. Then a question is posed: does Abu Hanifa allow sitting in the first rak'ah after starting standing? Yes, because the unrestricted nature (itlaq al-wad') indicates permissibility—i.e., the default is flexibility in nafl. The final part discusses a vow without specifying posture: some scholars say the person has a choice between sitting and standing, while others say standing is obligatory because Allah made obligatory prayers standing. This reflects an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa: one may sit in both rak'ahs of nafl if started standing, and a vow without specification gives a choice.

Key Terms
شروع (shuru'): Commencement of a supererogatory act of worship, which has legal implications but is not equivalent to a vow in binding force.
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship, making it wajib upon the person exactly as specified.
إطلاق وضع (itlaq al-wad'): The unrestricted nature of the act (i.e., the lack of specific condition), indicating permissibility of sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person starts a supererogatory prayer standing, what is the ruling on sitting in the first rak'ah?
A) It is not permissible under any circumstance.
B) It is permissible only if he had an excuse.
C) It is permissible, just as in the second rak'ah.
D) It is obligatory to stand again if he sits.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa distinguishes between shuru' and nadhr, allowing sitting in any rak'ah of a nafl prayer even if started standing.

Prayer on a Riding Animal: Nafl and Fard Rulings
States rulings and conditions for prayer on a riding animal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing supererogatory and obligatory prayer while riding an animal, and identify the valid excuses that permit obligatory prayer on a mount.

Core Idea
Nafl prayer on a mount is always permissible; fard prayer requires a genuine excuse.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira addresses a practical scenario for travelers: praying while riding an animal. It distinguishes between supererogatory (nafl) and obligatory (fard) prayers, providing the rationale of ease and listing specific excuses for fard. Understanding this ruling is essential for those who travel or face hardship, ensuring they know when they may pray on a mount and when they must dismount.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon: performing prayer on a riding animal. Note the two categories: nafl (supererogatory) and fard (obligatory). The ruling for nafl is unconditional permissibility; for fard, it is conditional.
The text begins with the general rule for nafl, then restricts fard.
2
Locate the proof and its type
The proof is rational (dalil aqli) based on hardship and benefit. The text cites al-Mabsut stating that even guarding the tongue from idle talk is a benefit. This shows the Hanafi use of maslaha and 'udhr.
No primary source (Qur'an/Hadith) is quoted; the reasoning is based on preventing harm (darar).
3
Trace the reasoning for nafl
Nafl is an act of goodness based on enthusiasm, not time-restricted. Requiring dismount and qiblah would cause the traveler to miss the caravan, causing harm. Hence, gestures and any direction suffice.
The phrase 'min al-manfa'ah' (from the benefit) indicates that even small benefit justifies the ruling.
4
List the excuses for fard
The text enumerates seven excuses: fear of predator/thief, mud/mire with no dry ground, restive animal requiring help to remount, old age with no assistance. In these cases, fard prayer on the mount is valid and does not require repetition.
The list is exhaustive in the text; other excuses may be analogized (qiyas).
5
Determine the consequences
When praying on a mount with excuse, the physical pillars (standing, bowing, prostration) are replaced by gestures (ima'), and facing the qiblah is also dropped. The prayer is valid and no i'adah (repetition) is needed.
This is the mufta bihi position as per al-Fatawa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن كان خارج المصر : يتنفّلُ على دابته إلى أي جهة توجهت، يومئ إيماء .
ولو افتتح التطوع قاعداً، ثم بدا له أن يقوم، فقام وصلى ما بقي: جاز عندهم جميعاً.
قوله: (ومن كان خارج المصر : يتنفل على دابته إلى أي جهة توجهت به، يومئ إيماء).
لأن النافلة خير موضوع مشروع على حسب النشاط، غير مختصة بوقت، فلو ألزمناه النزول واستقبال القبلة: تنقطع عنه القافلة، أو ينقطع هو عن القافلة، وكلاهما ضرر.
قال في «المبسوط (۱) : لو لم يكن له في التنفل على الدابة من المنفعة إلا حفظ اللسان من فضول الكلام: لكان كافياً.
وقيَّد بالنافلة ؛ لأن المكتوبة لا تجوز على الدابة، إلا من عذر، وهو أن يخاف من النزول على نفسه أو دابته، من سبع، أو لص، أو كان في طين، أو رَدَغَة لا يجد على الأرض مكاناً جافاً، أو كانت الدابة جموحاً لو نزل لا يُمكنه الركوب إلا بمُعين أو كان شيخاً كبيراً لو نزل: لا يمكنه الركوب ولا يجد مَن يُعينه : فتجوز صلاة الفرض في هذه الأحوال كلها على الدابة، ولا تلزمه الإعادة.
وكما تسقط الأركان عن الراكب يسقط عنه استقبال القبلة. كذا في «الفتاوى».
And whoever is outside the metropolis (misr): he may perform supererogatory prayer on his mount, facing whichever direction it turns, making gestures (ima'). And if he began the supererogatory prayer sitting, then it occurred to him to stand, and he stood and prayed the remainder: it is permissible according to all of them. His statement: (And whoever is outside the metropolis: he may perform supererogatory prayer on his mount, facing whichever direction it takes him, making gestures). Because the supererogatory prayer is a good act instituted according to enthusiasm, not restricted to a specific time; if we were to obligate him to dismount and face the qiblah, the caravan would leave him, or he would be separated from the caravan, and both are harmful. He said in 'al-Mabsut': If there were no benefit in performing supererogatory prayer on the mount except protecting the tongue from idle talk, that would be sufficient. And it is restricted to supererogatory prayer; because obligatory prayer is not permissible on a mount except with an excuse: that he fears for himself or his mount if he dismounts, from a predator or a thief, or he is in mud or mire such that he cannot find a dry place on the ground, or the mount is restive such that if he dismounts he cannot remount except with assistance, or he is a very old man who if he dismounts cannot remount and finds no one to assist him. In all these cases, obligatory prayer is permissible on the mount, and he is not required to repeat it. And just as the pillars (arkan) are dropped for the rider, so too is facing the qiblah dropped. As in al-Fatawa.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on performing supererogatory (nafl) prayer while riding an animal outside the built-up area (misr). The matn states: 'Whoever is outside the city may pray nafl on his mount facing any direction, making gestures.' The commentary explains the rationale: nafl is an act of goodness based on one's eagerness; it is not time-specific. If dismounting and facing the qiblah were required, the traveler might miss the caravan, causing hardship. Al-Mabsut even notes that the benefit of such prayer includes guarding the tongue from idle talk. This ruling applies only to nafl; obligatory prayers (fard) on a riding animal are not permissible except with a valid excuse. The excuses listed are: fear for oneself or the mount from predators or thieves, being in mud or mire with no dry ground, the animal being restive such that remounting without help is impossible, or old age with no assistance to remount. In these cases, fard prayer on the mount is valid and does not require repetition (i'rādah). Also, just as the physical pillars (like standing and bowing properly) are dropped, so is facing the qiblah dropped. This is the relied-upon position from the fatwa literature.

Key Terms
تتنفل (tatanaffalu): Performs supererogatory (nafl) prayer.
يومئ إيماء (yum'i ima'an): Makes gestures (substituting for bowing and prostration) when praying on a mount.
عذر ('udhr): Valid excuse that permits performing fard prayer on a mount, such as fear, mud, restive animal, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fear of a thief if you dismount.
B) The ground is muddy and no dry place is found.
C) You are feeling lazy and don't want to dismount.
D) The animal is restive and you cannot remount without help.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits nafl prayer on a mount unconditionally but restricts fard prayer on a mount to cases of genuine hardship as specified in the text.

Performing Nafl Prayer on a Riding Animal Outside the Town
Explains permissibility and conditions of nafl on riding animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing nafl prayer on a riding animal outside the town, identify the conditions and exceptions, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding performance inside the town.

Core Idea
Nafl on a riding animal outside town is permitted by istihsan to avoid hardship; inside town, the majority forbids it.

This passage from the commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar addresses a classic scenario: a traveler outside the town who wishes to perform supererogatory prayer while riding. The Hanafi school grants a concession, allowing nafl on the animal without facing the qibla or performing full bowing and prostration. However, this concession is carefully bounded—it applies only outside the town and only for nafl, not for obligatory prayers except in dire circumstances. This lesson unpacks the rule, its rationale (istihsan), the definition of 'outside the town,' and an intra-Hanafi difference of opinion regarding performance inside the town.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing nafl (supererogatory) prayer on a riding animal while outside the town. The ruling: it is permissible (jā'iz) and the act itself is sunnah. The rider may face any direction and nod (īmā') instead of bowing and prostrating.
The text explicitly restricts this to nafl; obligatory (fard) and witr are excluded.
2
Understand the dalil (istihsan)
The concession is based on istihsan (juristic preference): forcing the rider to dismount and face qibla would cause separation from the caravan, resulting in hardship. The text from al-Mabsut adds that even the benefit of avoiding idle talk is sufficient. This overrides the general requirement of facing qibla.
The dalil is 'aqli' (rational) and the proof is the harm (ḍarar) that would occur.
3
Note the exceptions for obligatory prayer
Obligatory (fard) prayer on a riding animal is only allowed in cases of genuine excuse: fear of predator/thief, deep mud, unruly animal, old age, etc. In these cases, the prayer is valid and need not be repeated.
The concession for fard is much narrower than for nafl.
4
Examine the definition of 'outside the town'
The 'town' (miṣr) refers to the built-up area. Outside is defined by the distance that permits a traveler to shorten prayers (qasr) – the most correct view. Alternative views include a mile or the Eid prayer ground, but the relied-upon position is the qasr distance.
The condition is location-based, not travel intent; one need not be a traveler to benefit from this concession.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Inside the town, Abu Hanifah and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) do not allow nafl on a riding animal, because the reason for the concession (separation from caravan) is absent. Abu Yusuf permits it. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the majority view of the two (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad).
The tarjih authority is the text itself, which states 'al-aṣaḥḥ' (the most correct) for the distance definition and 'indahumā' for the inside-town ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل
ومن كان خارج المصر : يتنفّلُ على دابته إلى أي جهة توجهت، يومي إيماء .
ولو افتتح التطوع قاعداً، ثم بدا له أن يقوم، فقام وصلى ما بقي: جاز عندهم جميعاً.
قوله: (ومن كان خارج المصر : يتنفل على دابته إلى أي جهة توجهت به، يومئ إيماء).
لأن النافلة خير موضوع مشروع على حسب النشاط، غير مختصة بوقت، فلو ألزمناه النزول واستقبال القبلة: تنقطع عنه القافلة، أو ينقطع هو عن القافلة، وكلاهما ضرر.
قال في «المبسوط»: لو لم يكن له في التنفل على الدابة من المنفعة إلا حفظ اللسان من فضول الكلام: لكان كافياً.
وقيَّد بالنافلة ؛ لأن المكتوبة لا تجوز على الدابة، إلا من عذر، وهو أن يخاف من النزول على نفسه أو دابته، من سبع، أو لص، أو كان في طين، أو رَدَغَة لا يجد على الأرض مكاناً جافاً، أو كانت الدابة جموحاً لو نزل لا يُمكنه الركوب إلا بمُعين أو كان شيخاً كبيراً لو نزل: لا يمكنه الركوب ولا يجد مَن يُعينه : فتجوز صلاة الفرض في هذه الأحوال كلها على الدابة، ولا تلزمه الإعادة.
وكما تسقط الأركان عن الراكب يسقط عنه استقبال القبلة. كذا في «الفتاوى».
الرَّدَعَة : بالتحريك، والغين المعجمة: الماء والطين والوحل الشديد، وكذا الرَّدْغَة : بالتسكين أيضاً، والجمع : رَدغ، ورداغ.
والوَحَل: بفتح الحاء : الطين الرقيق، وبتسكين الحاء: لغة رديئة. كذا في «الصحاح».
والسنن الرواتب: نوافل.
وعن أبي حنيفة : ينزل لسنة الفجر ؛ لأنها أكد من سائرها.
- والتقييد بخارج المصر: ينفي اشتراط السفر، وينفي الجواز في المصر.
وحد خارج المصر :
قيل : قَدْرُ الميل، فإن كان أقل من ذلك : لا يجوز.
وقيل: قدروه بمصلى العيد، والأصح أنه مقدر بما يجوز للمسافر القصر فيه.
ولو كان في المصر : لا يجوز له التنفل على الدابة عندهما.
وقال أبو يوسف: يجوز.
لهما: أن المتنفل إنما جُوِّز له ذلك ؛ لأن بالنزول ينقطع عن القافلة، وهذا المعنى معدوم في المصر.
قوله : يتنفل : يُحترز به عن الفرض والوتر.
Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers. And whoever is outside the town: he may perform supererogatory prayer on his riding animal in whatever direction it faces, nodding with his head. If he begins a voluntary prayer sitting, then it occurs to him to stand, so he stands and prays the remainder: it is permissible according to all of them. His statement: (And whoever is outside the town: he may perform supererogatory prayer on his riding animal in whatever direction it faces, nodding with his head). Because supererogatory prayer is a good act legislated according to convenience, not specific to a time. So if we oblige him to dismount and face the qibla, the caravan would leave him, or he would be separated from the caravan, and both are harmful. It is said in al-Mabsut: If there were no benefit in performing supererogatory prayer on the animal except preserving the tongue from excessive speech, that would be sufficient. And it is restricted to supererogatory prayer because obligatory prayer is not permissible on a riding animal except for an excuse: that he fears for himself or his animal from a predator or thief, or he is in mud or deep mud and cannot find a dry place on the ground, or the animal is unruly such that if he dismounts he cannot mount except with help, or he is a very old man such that if he dismounts he cannot mount and does not find anyone to help him. In all these situations, obligatory prayer is permissible on the riding animal and he is not required to repeat it. Just as the pillars are dropped for the rider, so too is facing the qibla dropped. Likewise in al-Fatawa. al-Rada‘ah: with vowel signs, with the ghayn: water, mud, and severe mire, and likewise al-radghah: with sukun also, plural radgh and radagh. al-Wahal: with fatha on the ha: thin mud, and with sukun on the ha: a bad language. Likewise in al-Sihah. The regular sunnah prayers are supererogatory. From Abu Hanifah: he dismounts for the sunnah of Fajr because it is more emphasized than others. And the restriction to outside the town negates the condition of travel and negates permissibility within the town. The definition of outside the town: some say a mile, and if less than that, it is not permissible. Some said it is defined by the Eid prayer ground, and the most correct is that it is defined by what permits a traveler to shorten prayers. And if he were in the town, it is not permissible for him to perform supererogatory prayer on the animal according to the two (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad). And Abu Yusuf said: it is permissible. Their proof: that the one performing supererogatory prayer is granted this concession because by dismounting he would be separated from the caravan, and this meaning is absent in the town. His statement: 'he performs supererogatory prayer' distinguishes from obligatory and witr prayer.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar deals with the rulings for performing nafl (supererogatory) prayers on a riding animal. The matn states: If one is outside the town, he may pray nafl on his riding animal in any direction, nodding. The commentator expands: The reason is that nafl is built on ease; forcing one to dismount and face qibla would cause separation from the caravan, causing harm. Quoting al-Mabsut, even the benefit of avoiding idle talk is sufficient. This ruling is specific to nafl; obligatory (fard) prayers are not allowed on an animal except for valid excuses like fear of predator/thief, deep mud, unruly animal, or old age. In such cases, the fard is valid and need not be repeated. The restriction to 'outside the town' means that travel itself is not a condition, but being within the town precludes this concession. The distance defining 'outside the town' is disputed: some say a mile, others the Eid prayer ground, but the most correct is the distance permitting qasr (shortening prayers) for travelers. Regarding the town, Abu Hanifah and Muhammad hold that nafl on a riding animal is not allowed, while Abu Yusuf allows it because the 'illa (reason of caravan separation) is absent in town. Additionally, Abu Hanifah says one should dismount for the sunnah of Fajr because it is more emphasized. The phrase 'he performs supererogatory prayer' excludes fard and witr from this ruling.

Key Terms
خارج المصر (khārij al-miṣr): Outside the town or city area; areas beyond the built-up limits.
إيماء (īmā'): Nodding with the head as a substitute for bowing and prostrating when praying on a riding animal.
السنن الرواتب (al-sunan al-rawātib): The regular sunnah prayers associated with the five daily obligatory prayers.
ردغة (radghah): Deep mud or mire; a condition that excuses performing fard on a riding animal.
مصلى العيد (muṣallā al-ʿīd): The Eid prayer ground, usually located outside the town.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reliable view (al-aṣaḥḥ) in the Hanafi school, what is the definition of 'outside the town' for permitting nafl on a riding animal?
A) A distance of one mile from the last building.
B) The location of the Eid prayer ground.
C) The distance at which a traveler may shorten prayers (qasr).
D) Any distance beyond the city limits.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits nafl prayer on a riding animal outside the town as a concession based on istihsan, but restricts it to nafl only; obligatory prayer requires a genuine excuse, and inside the town the majority does not permit it.

Rulings on Supererogatory Prayers While Riding: Conditions and Intra-Hanafi Disputes
Explaining the rules for nawafil on a mount, with definitions and intra-Hanafi disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi conditions for performing nafil prayer on a mount and identify the key intra-Hanafi disagreements.

Core Idea
Nafil on a mount is a concession limited to outside the city, with a dispute over its permissibility inside.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira details the rulings for supererogatory prayers while riding. After clarifying relevant vocabulary, the author presents the conditions required for the concession and records several intra-Hanafi disagreements, particularly between Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
The passage discusses tanafful (supererogatory prayer), excluding fard and witr. Understand that rawatib are considered nawafil.
Witr is wajib in the Hanafi school, so it is not included in nafil.
2
Locate the basic condition
The concession is restricted to outside the city (kharij al-misr) and only when the animal is moving.
The text explicitly says 'والتقييد بخارج المصر'.
3
Examine the proof for the condition
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that descending would separate one from the caravan, a concern absent inside the city.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli).
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf permits nafil on a mount inside the city, differing from the two. The text provides the two's proof but not Abu Yusuf's.
The relied-upon view is that of Abu Hanifa.
5
Apply the rulings to edge cases
Consider scenarios like entering the city while riding (invalidates according to Abu Hanifa), dismounting and remounting (much action requires restart), and the method of gestures.
These nuances are important for proper practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل
الرَّدَعَة : بالتحريك، والغين المعجمة: الماء والطين والوحل الشديد، وكذا الرَّدْغَة : بالتسكين أيضاً، والجمع : رَدغ، ورداغ.
والوَحَل: بفتح الحاء : الطين الرقيق، وبتسكين الحاء: لغة رديئة. كذا في «الصحاح».
والسنن الرواتب: نوافل.
وعن أبي حنيفة : ينزل لسنة الفجر ؛ لأنها أكد من سائرها.
- والتقييد بخارج المصر: ينفي اشتراط السفر، وينفي الجواز في المصر.
وحد خارج المصر :
قيل : قَدْرُ الميل، فإن كان أقل من ذلك : لا يجوز.
وقيل: قدروه بمصلى العيد، والأصح أنه مقدر بما يجوز للمسافر القصر فيه.
ولو كان في المصر : لا يجوز له التنفل على الدابة عندهما.
وقال أبو يوسف: يجوز.
لهما: أن المتنفل إنما جُوِّز له ذلك ؛ لأن بالنزول ينقطع عن القافلة، وهذا المعنى معدوم في المصر.
قوله : يتنفل : يُحترز به عن الفرض والوتر.
وإنما يجوز له التنفل على الدابة إذا كانت سائرة، أما إذا كانت واقفة : فلا.
ولو صلى الفرض على بعير قائم لا يسير: لا يجوز.
ولو صلى على عجل قائم لا يسير : جاز.
ولا يُشبه الحيوان العيدان. كذا في المنتقى.
وفي «الذخيرة : إذا صلى الفرض في شقِّ مَحْمَل على دابة، وركَزَ تحت المحمل خشبةً حتى صار قرار المحمل عليها: جاز.
ولو افتتح التطوع خارج المصر راكباً، ثم دخل المصر راكباً: بطلت تحريمته، حتى لو قهقه : لا وضوء عليه، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة.
وفي المرغيناني : يتمها على الدابة ما لم يبلغ منزله.
وقيل: ينزل، ويتمها نازلاً.
ولو افتتح التطوع راكباً، ثم نزل يبني وإن صلى ركعة نازلاً، ثم ركب يستأنف ؛ لأن الركوب عمل كثير.
وعند زفر : يبني في الوجهين.
قوله : إلى أي جهة توجهت به فإن صلى إلى غير ما توجهت به الدابة : لا يجوز؛ لعدم الضرورة. كذا في «الفتاوى».
- وقوله : يومىء إيماء: ويجعل السجود أخفض من الركوع.
Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers. al-Rada'ah (with vowel marks and غ with dots): water, mud, and thick mire, and likewise al-Radghah (with sukun also), plural: radgh and radagh. And al-Wahal (with fatha on ha): thin mud, and with sukun on ha: a bad dialect. Thus in al-Sihah. And the regular sunan are nawafil. And from Abu Hanifa: he descends for the sunnah of Fajr because it is more emphasized than others. And the restriction [in the text] to outside the city negates the condition of travel and negates permissibility inside the city. The definition of outside the city: some said it is a mile; if less than that, it is not allowed. And some said they estimated it as the place of the Eid prayer, and the correct [view] is that it is defined by what allows a traveler to shorten. And if he were inside the city, it is not permissible for him to perform supererogatory [prayer] on an animal according to the two [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad]. And Abu Yusuf said: it is permissible. Their [the two's] proof: that the one performing supererogatory prayer was only permitted that because descending causes him to be cut off from the caravan, and this meaning is absent in the city. His saying: 'he performs supererogatory [prayer]' is to exclude obligatory and witr. And it is only permissible for him to perform supererogatory on the animal if it is moving; if it is stationary: not allowed. And if he prays obligatory prayer on a standing camel that does not move: not allowed. And if he prays on a standing cart that does not move: it is allowed. And an animal is not like wood. Thus in al-Muntaqa. And in al-Dhakhira: if he prays obligatory prayer on the side of a litter on an animal and fixes a wood under the litter until the litter rests on it: it is allowed. And if he begins voluntary [prayer] outside the city riding, then enters the city riding: his tahrima is invalidated, such that if he laughs [in prayer], no wudu is required of him, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. And in al-Murghinani: he completes it on the animal as long as he has not reached his house. And it is said: he descends and completes it on foot. And if he begins voluntary [prayer] riding, then descends, he builds [continues], but if he prays one raka'ah on foot then mounts, he restarts, because mounting is a lot of action. And according to Zufar: he builds in both cases. His saying: 'to whichever direction it faces him' then if he prays to other than what the animal faces: not allowed due to lack of necessity. Thus in al-Fatawa. And his saying: 'he gestures with a gesture' and he makes prostration lower than bowing.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira covers the chapter on nawafil, specifically the rulings for performing supererogatory prayers while riding an animal. The author first clarifies vocabulary: رَدَعَة and رَدْغَة refer to mud and mire, and وَحَل to thin mud. He then notes that the regular sunan (rawatib) are considered nawafil. A key point from Abu Hanifa is that one should descend to pray the Fajr sunnah because it is the most emphasized of the rawatib. The main ruling concerns the permissibility of nafil on a mount: it is only allowed outside the city (مصر). The definition of 'outside' is debated: some say a mile, others the Eid prayer ground, but the relied-upon view is the distance allowing qasr. Inside the city, Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (عندهما) say it is not permissible, while Abu Yusuf permits it; their proof is the absence of the caravan concern (معنى القافلة) inside the city. The text emphasizes that the concession is only for nafil (excluding fard and witr) and only when the animal is moving. Obligatory prayer on a stationary camel is invalid, but on a stationary cart (عجل) it is valid because a cart is not like a living animal. Al-Dhakhira mentions a case where fixing a wood under a litter makes fard prayer valid. The passage then discusses the effect of entering the city: according to Abu Hanifa, starting nafil outside and then entering the city while riding invalidates the prayer's sanctity (تحريمة) to the extent that laughing does not require wudu. Al-Murghinani reports that one can continue until reaching home; others say descend and complete on foot. If one descends and then mounts again, the action of mounting is considered 'much action' so one must restart; Zufar disagrees, allowing continuation in both cases. Finally, the direction of the animal's movement determines the qibla, and gestures (إيماء) are used for bowing and prostration, with the latter being lower.

Key Terms
الرَّدَعَة (al-rada'ah): Water, mud, and thick mire (as defined in the text).
الرَّدْغَة (al-radghah): Same as al-rada'ah, with sukun on the letter.
الوَحَل (al-waḥal): Thin mud, with fatha on the حاء; the sukun form is a bad dialect.
السنن الرواتب (al-sunan al-rawātib): The regular voluntary prayers associated with the obligatory prayers (rawatib) – the text says these are nawafil.
تنفل (tanafful): Performing supererogatory (nafl) prayer, excluding fard and witr according to the text.
خارج المصر (khārij al-miṣr): Outside the city or town; defined as the distance where qasr becomes permissible (about a mile or the Eid prayer ground, but the relied-upon view is the qasr distance).
تحريمة (taḥrīmah): The state of ritual consecration (sanctity) upon beginning prayer; if invalidated, the prayer's ban on laughing etc. is lifted.
إيماء (īmā'): Gesture used during prayer on a mount to indicate bowing (rukū') and prostration (sujūd), with prostration being lower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling if a person begins a voluntary prayer while riding outside the city and then enters the city while still riding?
A) The prayer remains valid and he completes it.
B) The prayer is invalidated (batalat taḥrīmatuhu).
C) He must descend and finish the prayer on foot.
D) He may continue riding as long as he has not reached his house.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits nafil on a mount only outside the city when moving, using gestures; entering the city invalidates the prayer, though Abu Yusuf differed.

Rulings on Prayer While Riding: Moving vs. Stationary Animals
Rulings on prayers on moving vs stationary animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for performing voluntary and obligatory prayers on a riding animal (dābbah) and identify the conditions that make the prayer valid or invalid.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer requires motion; obligatory prayer requires stability — the animal's movement is treated differently from inanimate objects.

This passage from the chapter on Nawafil (voluntary prayers) sets out key rulings regarding prayer on riding animals. The Hanafi school distinguishes between voluntary and obligatory prayers, and between moving and stationary animals. Additionally, it introduces a principle that a living animal is not like an inanimate object, affecting the validity of prayer. In this lesson, we will unpack each ruling and the conditions that govern it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Determine whether the prayer being performed is voluntary (nafl) or obligatory (fard). The ruling varies accordingly.
Voluntary prayer is more flexible than obligatory prayer in these rulings.
2
Distinguish between moving and stationary animal
For voluntary prayer, the animal must be moving; if stationary, the prayer is invalid. For obligatory prayer, a stationary camel invalidates, but a stationary cart is valid.
The text introduces a maxim: 'The animal is not like wood' — living beings are inherently unstable.
3
Apply the 'animal vs. inanimate' maxim
Understand why a cart (inanimate) is treated differently from a camel (living). The ruling for obligatory prayer on an inanimate object is valid because it provides stability, while a living animal may shift.
This principle applies only to obligatory prayers; voluntary prayers are allowed on moving animals due to their lighter nature.
4
Consider the exception: litter with stick
If the litter (mahmal) is stabilized by a stick, obligatory prayer becomes valid. Recognize that artificial stability removes the prohibition.
This exception shows that the root cause (illah) is the animal's potential movement, not the animal itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما يجوز له التنفل على الدابة إذا كانت سائرة، أما إذا كانت واقفة : فلا.
ولو صلى الفرض على بعير قائم لا يسير: لا يجوز.
ولو صلى على عجل قائم لا يسير : جاز.
ولا يُشبه الحيوان العيدان. كذا في المنتقى».
وفي «الذخيرة : إذا صلى الفرض في شقِّ مَحْمَل على دابة، وركَزَ تحت المحمل خشبةً حتى صار قرار المحمل عليها: جاز.
He is only permitted to perform voluntary prayer on a riding animal when it is moving; as for when it is stationary: no. If he prays the obligatory prayer on a standing camel that does not walk: it is not valid. If he prays on a stationary cart: it is valid. The animal is not like wood. Thus in al-Muntaqa. And in al-Dhakhira: If he prays the obligatory prayer in a litter (mahmal) on an animal, and he fixes a stick under the litter so that the base of the litter rests on it: it is valid.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Nawafil states multiple rulings. First, voluntary prayer (nafl) on a riding animal is only permissible when the animal is moving (sa'ira). If the animal is stationary (waqifa), the prayer is invalid (la yajuz). Second, if one prays an obligatory prayer (fard) on a standing camel that does not walk, the prayer is invalid. Third, if one prays on a stationary cart (ajal), the prayer is valid because the cart is an inanimate object, unlike a living animal. The text notes a maxim from al-Muntaqa: the living animal is not like wood (i.e., its movement is part of the ruling). Finally, a quote from al-Dhakhira adds that if one prays obligatory prayer in a litter (mahmal) on an animal, and fixes a stick under the litter so that the base of the litter rests on the stick (making the position stable), the prayer is valid. These rulings emphasize the importance of stability and the absence of unnecessary movement during prayer.

Key Terms
دابة (dābbah): A riding animal (horse, mule, camel, etc.)
تنفل (tanafful): Voluntary supererogatory prayer
سائرة (sā'irah): Moving, in motion
محمل (maḥmil): A litter or sedan carried on an animal

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is a voluntary prayer on a riding animal valid?
A) Only when the animal is moving
B) Only when the animal is standing still
C) Both when moving and stationary
D) Only if the animal is a camel

Key Takeaway
Voluntary prayer is valid only on a moving animal; obligatory prayer requires a stable mount, whether inanimate or artificially stabilized.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Entering City While Riding During Voluntary Prayer
Dispute on tahrimah when entering city during voluntary prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the validity of voluntary prayer when re-entering a city while riding, identify the point of intra-Hanafi disagreement, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Tahrimah is lost when entering the city riding? Abu Hanifa says yes; others say no.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute about a worshipper who begins a voluntary prayer while riding outside the city limits and then rides into the city during the prayer. Does entering the city nullify the prayer's sanctity (tahrimah), or can one continue? The passage presents Abu Hanifa's view, alongside other positions from al-Murghinani and a general 'qila', and also addresses the cases of voluntarily descending and mounting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Variable
The act is a voluntary (nafl) prayer opened while riding outside a city (misr). The variable is entering the city while still riding.
The term 'misr' means a city or settled area; outside is considered travel territory.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position and Its Consequence
Abu Hanifa holds that the tahrimah (sanctity of prayer) is nullified upon entering the city riding. Consequence: if the worshipper laughs out loud (qahqaha), no wudu is needed because the prayer was already invalid.
Tahrimah refers to the state of inviolability initiated by the opening takbir.
3
Identify the Other Positions
Al-Murghinani reports one can complete the prayer on the animal until reaching home. Another view (qila) says descend and complete on the ground. These imply the prayer remains valid.
These positions represent the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and others.
4
Analyze the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: if the prayer is nullified (Abu Hanifa), no compensation needed for the invalid prayer; if not nullified, the worshipper may continue or descend and complete it, and the prayer counts as valid.
The passage does not give a tarjih, but later Hanafi works may prefer the view of completing on the animal.
5
Apply to the Scenarios of Descending and Mounting
If the worshipper voluntarily descends during the prayer, he may build upon (yabni) what he already performed. If he prays a rak'ah on the ground then mounts again, he must start over because mounting is a lot of action (amal kathir). Zufar holds he can build in both cases.
This shows additional intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf concerning continuity and change of posture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو افتتح التطوع خارج المصر راكباً، ثم دخل المصر راكباً: بطلت تحريمته، حتى لو قهقه : لا وضوء عليه، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة.
وفي المرغيناني : يتمها على الدابة ما لم يبلغ منزله.
وقيل: ينزل، ويتمها نازلاً.
ولو افتتح التطوع راكباً، ثم نزل يبني وإن صلى ركعة نازلاً، ثم ركب يستأنف ؛ لأن الركوب عمل كثير.
وعند زفر : يبني في الوجهين.
And if he begins voluntary prayer outside the city riding, then enters the city riding: his tahrimah (state of prayer) is nullified, such that if he laughs out loud, no wudu is required, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. In al-Murghinani: He completes it on the animal as long as he has not reached his home. Some say: He descends and completes it while descending. And if he begins voluntary prayer riding, then descends, he builds upon it; and if he prays a rak'ah descending, then mounts, he starts over because mounting is a lot of action. According to Zufar: He builds upon it in both cases.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation of a person who begins a voluntary prayer while riding outside the city (misr) and then enters the city while still riding. According to Abu Hanifa, the tahrimah (sanctity of prayer) is nullified (batalat). The consequence is that if he laughs out loud (qahqaha) during the prayer, he does not need to repeat wudu (since the prayer was already invalid). Other opinions: In al-Murghinani, the person completes the prayer on the animal as long as he does not arrive at his home. Another view says he should descend and complete it on the ground. If he voluntarily descends during the prayer, he can build (yabni) upon what he already performed. However, if after descending he rides again, he must start over because mounting is considered a lot of action (amal kathir) that breaks continuity. Zufar holds that he can build upon the prayer in both cases. This shows intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the effects of entering the city and changing modes of travel.

Key Terms
تحريمة (taḥrīmah): The state of sanctity/initiation of prayer; the opening takbir
مصر (miṣr): A city or settled area
قهقه (qahqaha): To laugh out loud (within prayer)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens if a person begins voluntary prayer outside the city riding and then enters the city riding?
A) The prayer remains valid
B) The tahrimah is nullified
C) He must repeat wudu
D) He must descend immediately

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has internal disagreement on whether entering a city while riding nullifies an already-opened voluntary prayer.
