Conditions for Obligation of Sajdah al-Sahw
Defines when sajdah al-sahw becomes wajib with commentary on key phrases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions (min jinsiha, laysa minha) that trigger sajdah al-sahw and apply them to classify actions in prayer as either obligating sajdah or not.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-sahw is wajib only when you add an action of prayer's genre that is not itself prescribed; lengthening a fard act does not trigger it.

Sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) is a wajib act that compensates for unintentional omissions, delays, or changes in prayer. But not every extra action triggers it. In this passage, the author of al-Jawhara al-Naira clarifies the precise conditions: the added action must be of the same genre as prayer (like standing, bowing, reciting) yet not part of the prayer's prescribed acts. This distinction ensures that lengthening a fard component, such as standing or sitting, does not necessitate sajdah. Understanding this saves one from unnecessary prostrations or from neglecting required ones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
The text begins by stating that sajdah al-sahw 'yalzamuhu' is incumbent. The commentary emphasises that this indicates wajib, not fard. Recognise that the Hanafi school grades sajdah as wajib, analogous to the sacrificial animals (dima) in Hajj.
The word 'yalzamuhu' is a clear indicator of wujub in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Extract the condition: 'min jinsiha'
The added action must be of the same genre as prayer (standing, bowing, prostrating, reciting, etc.). This excludes non‑ritual actions like moving stones or worldly speech. Such non‑jins actions either render the prayer makruh or invalidate it, but they do not trigger sajdah.
The commentary uses the example of 'taqlib al-hajar' (turning a stone).
3
Extract the condition: 'laysa minha'
The added action must not be from the prayer itself, meaning it must not be one of the prescribed acts (arkan or wajibat). Lengthening the standing or sitting, even though it adds time, is not considered an addition that requires sajdah because it is of the prayer and indeed fard.
The author answers a hypothetical question about the benefit of this phrase, showing its utility in excluding prescribed acts.
4
Understand the proof (qiyas)
The commentary draws an analogy (qiyas) to the sacrificial animals (dima) in Hajj. Just as dam is wajib to compensate for a deficiency in Hajj, sajdah al-sahw is wajib to compensate for a deficiency in prayer. Both are legislated for jabr (compensation).
This is a clear example of qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) used by the Hanafi school.
5
Note additional rulings and exceptions
The passage also mentions that if one returns to sajdah al-sahw and another follows him in prayer, it is valid. It also repeats the rule about qahqaha (loud laughter) requiring wudu, and notes that the sitting after sajdah is not fard but sunnah.
These are supplementary points; the core definition remains the two conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسجود السهو يلزم المصلي : إذا زاد في صلاته فعلاً من جنسها ليس منها . وأجمعوا أنه إذا عاد إلى سجدتي السهو، ثم اقتدى به رجل: صح اقتداؤه. وكذا إذا قهقه : يجب عليه الوضوء. قال في «الفتاوى»: القعدة بعد سجدتي السهو: ليست بفرض، وإنما أمر بها ليقع ختم الصلاة بها، حتى لو قام، وتركها: لا تفسد صلاته. كذا قال الحلواني. * قوله: (وسجود السهو يلزمه: إذا زاد في صلاته فعلاً من جنسها، ليس منها). في قوله: يلزمه: تصريح بأنه واجب، وهو الصحيح؛ لأنه شرع لجبر النقصان فكان واجباً كالدماء في الحج، وإذا كان واجباً: لا يجب إلا بترك واجب، أو بتأخيره، أو بتغيير ركن ساهياً. قوله : من جنسها احترز عن غير جنسها كتقليب الحجر، ونحوه، فإنه إما أن يكون مكروهاً، أو مفسداً. فإن قلت: ما الفائدة في قوله : ليس منها : إذ المعلوم أنه إذا زاد في صلاته : علم أن الزائد ليس منها؟ قلت: احترز بذلك عما إذا أطال القيام أو القعود: فإنه زاد فيها فعلاً من جنسها، وهو لا يوجب عليه سجود السهو؛ لأنه منها، بدليل أن ذلك فرض.
And the prostration of forgetfulness is incumbent upon the praying person: when he adds in his prayer an action of its type that is not from it. And they consensus that if he returns to the two prostrations of forgetfulness and then a man follows him, his following is valid. And likewise if he laughs loudly: wudu is obligatory upon him. He said in al-Fatawa: The sitting after the two prostrations of forgetfulness is not a fard; rather it is commanded so that the seal of the prayer occurs with it, such that if he stands and leaves it, it does not invalidate his prayer. Thus said al-Halwani. His statement: (And the prostration of forgetfulness is incumbent upon him: when he adds in his prayer an action of its type that is not from it). In his statement 'incumbent upon him': a declaration that it is wajib, and that is the correct view because it is legislated to compensate for deficiency, so it is wajib like the sacrificial animals in Hajj. And when it is wajib, it becomes obligatory only by leaving a wajib, or delaying it, or changing a rukun inadvertently. His statement 'of its type' excludes that which is not of its type, like turning over a stone and similar, for it is either makrooh or invalidating. If you say: what is the benefit in his statement 'not from it' — knowing that if he adds to his prayer, one knows that the added thing is not from it? I say: he excludes by that the lengthening of standing or sitting, for he has added an action of its type, but it does not obligate sajdah al-sahw upon him because it is from it, with the evidence that that is fard.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage provides the foundational definition for when sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) becomes obligatory (wajib). The key condition is: if a person adds in his prayer an action that is 'of its type' (min jinsiha) and 'not from it' (laysa minha). The commentary then elaborates. First, the word 'yalzamuhu' confirms that sajdah al-sahw is wajib, not sunnah, because it is legislated to compensate for a deficiency, analogous to the sacrificial animals (dima') in Hajj. It is only required when a wajib act is omitted, delayed, or a rukun is inadvertently changed. The phrase 'min jinsiha' excludes actions that are not of the same genre as prayer, like moving a stone; such actions are either makrooh or invalidating (mufsid). The phrase 'laysa minha' clarifies that prolonging the standing or sitting, even though it adds time, is not considered an added action that requires sajdah because it is part of the prayer (minha) and indeed it is fard (obligatory) to stand and sit. So, increasing the amount of a fard act does not trigger sajdah al-sahw. Additionally, the text notes consensus on the validity of iqtida after the imam returns to sajdah al-sahw, and repeats the rule about qahqaha. It also mentions that the sitting after the two prostrations is not fard but only recommended for sealing the prayer.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness or mistake in prayer.
من جنسها (min jinsiha): Of the same genre as the prayer (e.g., standing, bowing, prostrating, reciting).
ليس منها (laysa minha): Not from the prayer itself, i.e., not part of the prescribed acts.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-sahw is wajib only when a person adds an action of the same genre as prayer that is not itself prescribed, as proven by qiyas to the dam in Hajj.

When Sajdah al-Sahw is Wajib Due to Addition of a Similar Act
Explanation of when sajdah al-sahw becomes wajib due to adding an act of the same genre.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for sajdah al-sahw when an act is added in prayer and explain why the Hanafi school considers it wajib using qiyas.

Core Idea
Increase in its improper place is a deficiency requiring sajdah al-sahw.

The prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw) is a wajib act that compensates for deficiencies in prayer. This lesson focuses on one specific cause: adding an act of the same genre as prayer (like an extra ruku or sujud) that is not originally part of the prayer. Understanding the precise condition—'of its genre but not from it'—is essential to correctly apply this ruling and avoid common misconceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The author states that sajdah al-sahw is obligatory (lazim) when a worshiper adds an act in prayer. Note the term 'lazim' which clearly indicates wujub.
This is the relied-upon Hanafi position, supported by the text's declaration 'wa huwa al-sahih'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to blood offerings (al-dima') in Hajj. Both sajdah and blood offerings are prescribed to compensate for deficiency; therefore, the ruling of wujub transfers from Hajj to salah.
This is a jali (clear) qiyas: the illa (effective cause) is compensation for deficiency.
3
Understand the condition 'min jinsiha wa laysa minha'
The addition must be an act 'of its genre' (like standing, bowing, prostrating) but 'not from it' (i.e., not the original prescribed acts). Excluded are acts not of the genre (e.g., moving a stone) and acts that are part of the prayer (e.g., prolonging standing).
This two-part condition ensures that only genuine additions trigger sajdah.
4
Address the objection: increase vs deficiency
The author anticipates a question: why does an increase require compensation for deficiency? The answer: an increase in the wrong place is itself a deficiency, illustrated by the analogy of a slave with an extra finger—an extra is a defect.
This shows the legal reasoning (talil) behind the ruling.
5
Distinguish from other related rulings
The passage also mentions that returning to sajdah is valid for following an imam, laughter requires wudu, and the sitting after sajdah is not fard but a seal. These are independent rulings; the core lesson is about the addition condition.
These sub-rulings do not affect the main condition but are worth noting.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

* قوله: (وسجود السهو يلزمه: إذا زاد في صلاته فعلاً من جنسها، ليس منها).
في قوله: يلزمه: تصريح بأنه واجب، وهو الصحيح؛ لأنه شرع لجبر النقصان فكان واجباً كالدماء في الحج، وإذا كان واجباً: لا يجب إلا بترك واجب، أو بتأخيره، أو بتغيير ركن ساهياً.

فإن قلت: لم وجب سجود السهو عند الزيادة، وإنما هو لجبر النقصان، والزيادة ضد النقصان؟
قلت: لأن الزيادة في غير موضعها : نقصان، ألا ترى أن من اشترى عبداً وله ست أصابع كان له رده ، كما لو كان له أربع أصابع. واعلم أن سجدتي السهو يجبران النقصان، ويُرضيان الرحمن، ويُرغمان الشيطان، فلهذا هما واجبتان.
Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness. And prostration of forgetfulness is obligatory for the prayer: if he adds an act in his prayer that is of its genre but not part of it. His following? And they have consensus that if he returns to the two prostrations of forgetfulness, then a man follows him, it is valid. Likewise, if he guffaws, wudu becomes obligatory upon him. In his saying 'obligatory for him' is a declaration that it is wajib, and this is correct; because it is legislated to compensate for deficiency, so it is wajib like the blood offerings in Hajj. And if it is wajib, it is not obligatory except due to leaving a wajib, or delaying it, or changing a rukun forgetfully. His saying: 'of its genre' is a precaution against what is not of its genre like turning over a stone and the like, for it is either makruh or invalidating. If you say: What is the benefit in his saying 'not from it' since it is known that if he adds in his prayer, it is known that the addition is not from it? I say: He guarded by that against when he prolongs the standing or sitting: for he added in it an act of its genre, and it does not obligate sajdah al-sahw upon him; because it is from it, as evidence that that is fard. If you say: Why is sajdah al-sahw obligated upon increase, whereas it is only to compensate for deficiency, and increase is opposite to deficiency? I say: Because increase in its improper place is deficiency. Do you not see that whoever buys a slave who has six fingers, he has the right to return him, just as if he had four fingers. And know that the two prostrations of forgetfulness compensate for deficiency, please the Most Merciful, and enrage the devil, so for this they are both wajib.

Commentary
This first lesson covers the primary ruling on sajdah al-sahw when one adds an action in prayer. The author begins by stating that sajdah al-sahw is mandatory (لازم) for the one praying when he adds an act of the same genre (من جنسها) that is not originally from prayer (ليس منها). This includes acts like an extra rak'ah or an extra sujud. The commentary clarifies that 'لازم' explicitly indicates wujub, which is the correct view. The reason is that sajdah al-sahw is prescribed to compensate for deficiency, so it is wajib by analogy with blood offerings (الدماء) in Hajj which are wajib for similar compensation. The condition 'of its genre' excludes acts not of prayer, like moving a stone, which either invalidate prayer or are makruh. The phrase 'not from it' excludes prolonging standing or sitting, which are from prayer and thus do not require sajdah. The author then addresses a question: why should increase require sajdah if it is meant for deficiency? The answer is that increase in the wrong place is itself a deficiency, illustrated by the analogy of a slave with six fingers—an extra is a defect justifying return. The lesson also includes two additional related rulings: the validity of following an imam who returns to sajdah al-sahw, and the requirement of wudu for laughing inside prayer. The fatwa from Al-Halwani states that the sitting after the two prostrations is not fard but a recommended seal. The note concludes that the two prostrations compensate deficiency, please Allah, and anger Satan, hence they are wajib.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
من جنسها (min jinsiha): Of the same genre, meaning acts of prayer (like ruku, sujud, qiyam).
يلزمه (yulzimuhu): It is obligatory upon him (used to indicate wujub).

Key Takeaway
An added act of prayer that is not originally part of it is a deficiency requiring sajdah al-sahw, by analogy to blood offerings in Hajj.

intermediate
6 min
Sajdah al-Sahw for Omission of Sunnah Acts and Fatiha
Explains when sajdah al-sahw is wajib due to omission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when omitting a sunnah act (wajib by Sunnah) or Surah al-Fatiha requires sajdah al-sahw according to the Hanafi school, and distinguish exceptions for dhikr.

Core Idea
Not every omission triggers sajdah—only leaving a wajib act or Fatiha, with five exceptions for dhikr.

In the Hanafi school, sajdah al-sahw compensates for forgetful omissions in prayer. This passage clarifies exactly which omissions require it: leaving a 'sunnah act' (meaning a wajib established by the Sunnah) and leaving Surah al-Fatiha. It also notes that forgetting ordinary remembrances does not require sajdah, except in five specific instances. Understanding this distinction ensures your prayer is corrected properly without unnecessary prostrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main causes
The passage lists two triggers for sajdah al-sahw: leaving a 'sunnah act' and leaving the recitation of Surah al-Fatiha (or most of it).
The 'sunnah act' is defined in the commentary as a wajib act known from the Sunnah.
2
Define 'sunnah act' in this context
The term 'sunnah act' (fi'l masnun) here refers specifically to an act whose obligation is proven by the Sunnah, not a nafl sunnah. Examples include the first sitting, standing instead of sitting, and leaving the prostration of recitation.
This is a Hanafi technical usage; other madhhabs may use different classifications.
3
Recognize the exceptions for dhikr
Forgetfulness regarding ordinary dhikr (thana, ta'awwudh, tasbih of ruku and sujud) does not require sajdah. However, five exceptions are mentioned: Eid takbirs, qunut, tashahhud, recitation (beyond Fatiha), and delaying the salam.
These five have a higher status and their omission does require sajdah.
4
Apply the ruling for Fatiha and majority rule
Leaving Surah al-Fatiha entirely or most of it requires sajdah because Fatiha is wajib. The principle 'the majority has the ruling of the whole' applies: if one leaves more than half, it is as if the entire recitation was left.
This reflects the Hanafi view that Fatiha is wajib, not fard.

That is, an obligatory act the obligation of which is known by the Sunnah, like the first sitting, or standing in the place of sitting, or leaving the prostration of recitation from its place. Commentary
This lesson covers the two causes of sajdah al-sahw related to omission. The first is leaving a 'sunnah act' (فعلاً مسنوناً), which here means an act that is wajib based on evidence from the Sunnah. Examples include the first sitting (القعدة الأولى) in a four-rak'ah prayer, standing instead of sitting after the first tashahhud, or leaving the prostration of recitation (سجدة التلاوة) when it is due. The author specifies that forgetfulness regarding mere remembrances (الأذكار) such as thana, ta'awwudh, and tasbih of ruku and sujud does not require sajdah al-sahw. However, there are five exceptions: the takbirs of 'Eid prayer, qunut (in witr), tashahhud, recitation (القراءة), and delaying the final salam from its proper time. The second cause is leaving the recitation of Surah al-Fatiha entirely or leaving most of it, because Fatiha is wajib in prayer according to the Hanafi school, and the majority takes the rule of the whole.

Key Terms
فعلاً مسنوناً (fi'l masnun): An act the obligation of which is established by the Sunnah (i.e., a waajib act).
القعدة الأولى (al-qa'dah al-ula): The first sitting after two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer
فاتحة الكتاب (Fatihah al-kitab): Surah al-Fatiha

Causes of Sajdat al-Sahw: Leaving Wajibat (Qunut, Tashahhud, Takbirat al-`Idayn)
Explains that leaving wajibat like qunut, tashahhud, and takbirat al-`idayn necessitates sajdat al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which wajibat in prayer require sajdat al-sahw and apply the ruling to recitation scenarios involving al-Fatiha and surah.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, leaving a wajib requires sajdat al-sahw – the prayer is valid but compensated.

When we forget a wajib element in prayer, the prayer does not become invalid. Instead, the Hanafi school requires sajdat al-sahw as compensation. This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah identifies three specific wajibat — qunut, tashahhud, and takbirat al-`idayn — and explores related scenarios to clarify when sajdah is and is not required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wajibat listed
List the three specific wajibat mentioned: qunut (in witr), tashahhud (final), and takbirat al-`idayn (extra takbirs in 'Eid prayer).
Each is followed by 'because it is wajib' indicating the ratio legis.
2
Note the ratio legis
For each wajib, the author states 'because it is wajib'. This means the sole reason sajdat al-sahw is required is the wajib status of the omitted act.
In Hanafi fiqh, wajib is a distinct category below fard; omission of wajib due to forgetfulness requires sajdah, not invalidation.
3
Analyze the recitation scenarios
Examine the cases involving al-Fatiha and surah in the first two rak'ahs, the last two rak'ahs, and the case of surah al-Sajdah. Determine when sajdah is required and when it is not.
Key principle: delaying the surah (by repeating Fatiha) triggers sajdah, but repeating Fatiha after the surah does not.
4
Apply the principle to related cases
Extend to the omitted takbir of ruku' in 'Eid prayer and the case of forgetting qunut. The same logic applies: any omitted wajib requires sajdat al-sahw.
The passage also mentions that in the last two rak'ahs, reciting Fatiha twice does not require sajdah because the recitation is optional.

His statement: (Or the qunut); because it is wajib.
Similarly if he leaves the takbir of qunut.
His statement: (Or the tashahhud); because it is wajib.

- If he recited al-Fatiha twice in the last two rak'ahs: no sajdat al-sahw.
If he recited al-Fatiha and the surah forgetfully in the last two rak'ahs: no sajdat al-sahw.
If he did not recite al-Fatiha in the second pair (of rak'ahs): no sajdat al-sahw; because he has a choice: if he wishes he recites, if he wishes he glorifies, if he wishes he is silent.
If he prayed with a surah of sajdah, and when he prostrated he stood and recited al-Fatiha forgetfully: sajdat al-sahw is required. Likewise in al-Waqi'at.

Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from the matn of Mukhtasar al-Quduri on the causes of sajdat al-sahw. The author first lists three wajibat whose omission triggers sajdat al-sahw: qunut, tashahhud, and the takbirat of the two 'Eid prayers. He explains each with the reason 'because it is wajib' — meaning that these acts are obligatory (wajib) in the Hanafi hierarchy, and forgetting them requires compensation via prostration. He adds that leaving the takbir of ruku' in 'Eid prayer also requires sajdah. Then he discusses various scenarios regarding recitation of al-Fatiha and surah: if one recites al-Fatiha twice in the first two rak'ahs, sajdat al-sahw is required because the surah was delayed; but if one recites al-Fatiha, then the surah, then al-Fatiha again forgetfully, no sajdah is needed because the order was still maintained. In the last two rak'ahs, repeating al-Fatiha or adding a surah forgetfully does not require sajdah, as the worshiper has the option to recite, glorify, or remain silent. Finally, if a person prays a surah containing an obligatory sajdah (like Surah al-Sajdah), and after prostrating rises and recites al-Fatiha forgetfully, sajdat al-sahw is required — this ruling is cited from al-Waqi'at. The end of the passage is corrupt but likely relates to recitation of the verse.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer; specifically for omitting a wajib or for certain types of errors.
القنوت (al-qunut): A specific supplication recited in the witr prayer or at times of calamity; here referring to the qunut of witr.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited in the sitting position of prayer; here referring to the final tashahhud.
تكبيرات العيدين (takbirat al-`idayn): The additional takbirs recited in 'Eid prayers; here meaning the extra takbirs at the beginning of each rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) No sajdat al-sahw is required
D) He must repeat the prayer after the time

Key Takeaway
Leaving a wajib in prayer — such as qunut, tashahhud, or takbirat al-`idayn — requires sajdat al-sahw to compensate, according to the Hanafi school.

Imam's Voice and Sajdat al-Sahw: Wajib, Dispute, and Followership
Rulings on jahr/ikhfat and forgetfulness in sajdat al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdat al-sahw for an imam's error in jahr/ikhfat, explain the dispute regarding the munfarid, and apply the rules of followership.

Core Idea
Imam's voice error is wajib that requires sajdat al-sahw; munfarid's jahr in sirri is disputed—only significant amounts.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira addresses an important aspect of sajdat al-sahw: when the imam raises or lowers his voice incorrectly, and how forgetfulness affects the imam and follower. You will learn that the imam's error in jahr/ikhfat is from the wajibat, and that the munfarid (individual) has a different ruling. The passage also clarifies that the follower's forgetfulness does not obligate any sajdah, while the imam's forgetfulness obligates the follower to follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wajibat of jahr and ikhfat
First, understand that jahr in jahri prayers and ikhfat in sirri prayers are wajibat for the imam. The source states: 'لأن الجهر في موضعه والمخافتة في موضعها: من الواجبات.' Omission of a wajib requires sajdat al-sahw.
This is a key principle: any omission of a wajib in salah triggers sajdat al-sahw.
2
Analyze the imam's error and the follower's obligation
If the imam errs in jahr/ikhfat, he must perform sajdat al-sahw, and the follower must follow him. If the imam does not prostrate, the follower cannot prostrate alone because he must follow the imam.
The follower's prayer is valid only when following the imam; opposing breaks the followership.
3
Examine the munfarid's situation: consensus on ikhfat
For the munfarid (individual), lowering voice in a jahri prayer (e.g., Fajr) requires no sajdah by consensus ('إجماعاً') because he has a choice. This is settled.
Consensus (ijma') makes this ruling definitive.
4
Explore the dispute on munfarid's jahr in sirri
When the munfarid raises his voice in a sirri prayer (e.g., Zuhr), there is disagreement. Al-Karkhi says no sajdah; al-Nawadir says sajdah is required. The soundest view (al-asahh) is that if the amount is significant enough to validate the prayer (one verse by Abu Hanifa, three by the Sahibayn), sajdat al-sahw is wajib.
The dispute is about quantity: what constitutes 'significant'? The 'asahh' view uses the threshold of validity.
5
Apply the rules of forgetfulness between imam and ma'mum
If the imam forgets, the ma'mum must perform sajdat al-sahw with him. If the ma'mum forgets, neither is obligated; this is because the ma'mum's independent sajdah would be opposing, and the imam cannot become a follower.
This principle preserves the hierarchy of the congregation.

Source Text

And the forgetfulness of the imam obligates the follower to prostrate; if the imam does not prostrate, the follower does not prostrate.
If the follower forgets, neither the imam nor the follower is obligated to prostrate.

And if he raises his voice in what should be lowered: there is disagreement among the scholars (mashayikh):
In al-Karkhi: no sajdat al-sahw is required.
And they differed over the quantity; the soundest view is the amount that makes the prayer valid in the two cases (jahri and sirri); because a little bit of raising and lowering cannot be avoided, but a lot can be, and what makes the prayer valid is a lot, except that according to Abu Hanifa it is one verse, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is three verses.
And in al-Nawadir: if the individual raises his voice in what should be lowered, sajdat al-sahw is required.

His statement: (And if the follower forgets, neither the imam nor the follower is obligated to prostrate); because if he prostrates alone, he becomes opposed to his imam, and if the imam follows him, the original (imam) becomes a follower.

Commentary
This passage from the sharh discusses two main issues: (1) the imam's raising or lowering his voice as a cause for sajdat al-sahw, and (2) the effect of forgetfulness of the imam and ma'mum (follower). The author explains that the imam's error in jahr/ikhfat is from the wajibat, hence requires sajdat al-sahw. However, for the munfarid (individual praying alone), lowering the voice in a jahri prayer requires no sajdah by consensus because he has a choice. But raising the voice in a sirri prayer is disputed: according to al-Karkhi, no sajdah; according to al-Nawadir, sajdah is wajib. The reliable view is that if the amount of jahr/ikhfat is enough to make the prayer valid (i.e., a minimal recitation), then it is considered significant; Abu Hanifa says one verse, the two disciples say three verses. Then the text addresses the relationship between imam and ma'mum: if the imam forgets, the ma'mum must follow him in sajdat al-sahw. If the imam does not prostrate, the ma'mum cannot prostrate alone because that would be opposing. If the ma'mum forgets, neither he nor the imam perform sajdat al-sahw, because if the ma'mum prostrates alone he opposes, and if the imam follows, the roles are reversed.

Key Terms
الجهر (al-jahr): Raising the voice in recitation, required in Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, Jumu'ah, and 'Eid prayers.
المخافتة (al-mukhafatah): Lowering the voice in recitation, required in Zuhr and Asr prayers.
المنفرد (al-munfarid): A person praying alone, not in congregation; he has more freedom in voice level.
المؤتم (al-mu'tamm): The follower (ma'mum) in congregational prayer; he must follow the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The imam must perform sajdat al-sahw on behalf of the follower

Key Takeaway
The imam's error in jahr/ikhfat is a wajib omission requiring sajdat al-sahw, but the munfarid's jahr in sirri is disputed based on quantity; the follower must follow the imam and cannot act independently.

Rulings on the Follower's Sujud al-Sahw in Congregational Prayer
Ruling on obligations of imam and follower in sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on sujud al-sahw for the imam and follower, and apply the principle that the follower must follow the imam in sujud al-sahw.

Core Idea
The follower must only perform sujud al-sahw when the imam does; the follower's own forgetfulness imposes no obligation.

This lesson examines the specific rulings of sujud al-sahw in congregational prayer. You will learn when the follower is required to prostrate and when he is not, based on the Hanafi principle that the follower's obligation is to follow the imam. Understanding these rules prevents invalidating the prayer by opposing the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage covers three cases: (1) Imam forgets and performs sujud al-sahw. (2) Imam forgets but does not perform sujud al-sahw. (3) Follower forgets.
2
Apply the obligation to follow
The follower is obligated to follow the imam in all actions. Therefore, the imam's action dictates the follower's action regarding sujud al-sahw.
Sujud al-sahw is wajib for the imam when he forgets; it becomes wajib for the follower when the imam performs it.
3
Determine the ruling for each scenario
Scenario 1: Follower must prostrate with the imam. Scenario 2: Follower must not prostrate. Scenario 3: Neither imam nor follower is obligated to prostrate.
4
Understand the rationale
The follower commits only to follow. Prostrating alone or leading the imam in sujud al-sahw opposes the imam and invalidates the follower's prayer.

قوله: (وإن سها المؤتم: لم يلزم الإمام ولا المؤتم السجود)؛ لأنه إذا سجد وحده: كان مخالفاً لإمامه، وإن تابعه الإمام: ينقلب الأصل تبعاً.
Chapter of Sujud al-Sahw. And the forgetfulness of the imam necessitates prostration for the follower; if the imam does not prostrate, the follower does not prostrate. And if the follower forgets, neither the imam nor the follower is obligated to prostrate. * His saying: (And the forgetfulness of the imam necessitates prostration for the follower) because following the imam is obligatory. * His saying: (If the imam does not prostrate, the follower does not prostrate) because if he prostrates alone, he becomes opposing his imam, and he only undertook prayer as a follower. His saying: (And if the follower forgets, neither the imam nor the follower is obligated to prostrate) because if he prostrates alone, he would be opposing his imam, and if the imam follows him, the follower becomes the leader.
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayirah commentary on Al-Mukhtasar al-Quduri addresses the rulings of sujud al-sahw in congregational prayer. It states that if the imam forgets, the follower is required to prostrate with him, because following the imam is obligatory. However, if the imam does not prostrate, the follower must not prostrate alone, as that would be opposing the imam, and the follower has committed only to following. Conversely, if the follower forgets, no sujud al-sahw is required from either the imam or the follower. If the follower prostrates alone, he opposes the imam; if the imam follows him, the roles are reversed (the follower becomes the leader). This ruling is based on the principle that the follower's obligation is to follow the imam in all actions.

Key Terms
سهو (sahw): Forgetfulness occurring in prayer.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for forgetfulness.
مؤتم (mu'tam): Follower in congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the imam forgets and does not perform sujud al-sahw, what should the follower do?
A) The follower should perform sujud al-sahw alone.
B) The follower should not perform sujud al-sahw.
C) The follower should remind the imam.
D) The follower should repeat the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The follower's sujud al-sahw is contingent on the imam's action; the follower's own forgetfulness does not require sujud.

Sujud al-Sahw for the Solitary Person: Jahri/Sirri Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on solitary person's sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether a solitary person performs sujud al-sahw for raising voice in silent prayer and identify the threshold amounts according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A solitary person has choice in jahri/sirri, but raising voice in silent prayer triggers a dispute on sujud al-sahw among Hanafi masters.

In this passage, the author explains why the rule for sujud al-sahw in jahri/sirri mistakes is restricted to the imam. For the solitary person, lowering voice in a jahri prayer is excused by consensus. However, raising voice in a sirri prayer leads to an intra-Hanafi dispute: is sujud al-sahw required, and what amount of jahr triggers it? This lesson unpacks the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Al-Karkhi, and identifies the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify consensus and disputed scenario
First, note the consensus: if a solitary person lowers his voice where it should be raised (jahri prayer), there is no sujud al-sahw. The dispute arises only when he raises his voice in a prayer where it should be lowered (sirri prayer).
The text says 'إجماعاً' (by consensus) for the first case.
2
Map the positions on obligation
According to Al-Karkhi, there is no sujud al-sahw at all. According to the Nawadir report, sujud is obligatory (wajib). The text indicates that the relied-upon view leans toward obligation when the amount is substantial.
The Nawadir is considered a reliable report in the Hanafi school, though not part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Compare thresholds between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa holds that one verse of audible recitation is enough to trigger sujud al-sahw. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani require three verses. The difference turns on whether a small amount can be avoided – a small amount is excused, but what renders prayer valid (a larger amount) is not.
The text calls the latter 'al-asahh' (most correct) regarding amount.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The text does not explicitly resolve the dispute, but indicates that the amount that renders prayer valid is the threshold (i.e., the same as for imam). For the obligation itself, the Nawadir view is often given weight in later fatwa, but the Karkhi view remains an alternative.
In practice, many later Hanafi jurists advise sujud al-sahw for the solitary person if a significant amount (more than one verse) is recited audibly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما قيد بالإمام: لأن المنفرد إذا خافت فيما يُجهر فيه: لا سهو عليه، إجماعاً؛ لأنه مخيّر. وإن جهر فيما يخافت فيه: ففيه اختلاف المشايخ : وفي الكرخي»: لا سهو عليه. واختلف في المقدار والأصح أنه قدر ما تجوز به الصلاة في الفصلين؛ لأن اليسير من الجهر والإخفاء : لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه، ويمكن عن الكثير، وما تصح به الصلاة كثير، غير أن ذلك عند أبي حنيفة: آية واحدة، وعندهما: ثلاث آيات. وفي «النوادر» : إذا جهر المنفرد فيما يخافت فيه: وجب عليه السهو.
And indeed he restricted with the imam because the solitary person, if he lowers his voice where it should be raised, there is no sujud upon him, by consensus, because he is given choice. And if he raises his voice where it should be lowered, there is difference among the mashayikh: according to Al-Karkhi: there is no sujud upon him. And they differed regarding the amount, and the correct view is that it is the amount by which the prayer is valid for the two contexts; because a slight amount of raising or lowering cannot be avoided, but a large amount can be avoided, and what renders the prayer valid is much, except that according to Abu Hanifa it is one verse, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is three verses. And in Al-Nawadir: if the solitary person raises his voice where it should be lowered, sujud is obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage discusses the case of a person praying alone (munfarid) regarding jahri (audible) and sirri (silent) recitation. The text explains why 'imam' was specified: because for a solitary person, if he reads silently in a prayer where recitation should be audible, there is no sujud al-sahw by consensus, as he has choice. However, if he reads audibly where it should be silent, there is ikhtilaf among later scholars (mashayikh). According to Al-Karkhi, no sujud. They also differed on the amount that triggers sujud: the correct view is the amount that would render the prayer valid in either context. A small amount is excused, a large amount is not. The minimum amount: according to Abu Hanifa, one verse; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, three verses. Additionally, the Nawadir report states that sujud is obligatory if the solitary person raises voice in a silent prayer.

Key Terms
منفرد (munfarid): A person praying alone (not as imam or follower).
جهر (jahr): Audible recitation in prayer.
إخفاء (ikhfa'): Silent recitation in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) One verse according to Abu Hanifa, three according to Sahibayn
C) One rukn
D) The amount that invalidates the prayer

Key Takeaway
The solitary person's sujud al-sahw for jahr in sirri prayer is disputed within the Hanafi school; the mufta bihi often follows the Nawadir (obligation) with a threshold of three verses as the precautionary view.

Forgetting the First Sitting: When to Return and When to Prostrate
States ruling and discusses intra-Hanafi dispute on sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for forgetting the first sitting based on proximity to sitting or standing, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding sujud al-sahw when returning near.

Core Idea
If near sitting, return and no sujud if you return; if near standing, continue and do sujud al-sahw.

Forgetting the first sitting (qa'dah ula) is a common occurrence in prayer. The Hanafi school provides a clear threshold based on whether you are closer to sitting or standing when you remember. But what happens if you return while still near sitting? Scholars differ on whether sujud al-sahw is needed. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its rationale, and the intra-madhhab disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling threshold
The source passage states that if one forgets the first sitting and remembers while closer to sitting (i.e., knees still on ground), he should return, sit, and recite tashahhud. If closer to standing (i.e., after fully standing), he does not return and performs sujud al-sahw.
The threshold is defined in Al-Mabsut as not yet being fully upright.
2
Understand the qiyas principle
The commentator explains the ruling using the principle 'what is near to a thing takes its ruling', analogous to the periphery of a city taking the city's ruling for Eid and Jumu'ah prayers.
This qiyas jaliy establishes that proximity to sitting treats the forgetful person as still sitting.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on sujud al-sahw
Al-Quduri did not mention sujud al-sahw when returning near. Al-Hidayah holds the correct view is no sujud. Al-Nihayah and Al-Makki hold that sujud is required. The dispute revolves around whether the wajib of sitting has been truly left if one returns quickly.
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether to add two extra prostrations at the end of the prayer.
4
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
Consider a person in Dhuhr prayer who forgets the first sitting and remembers just as he is straightening his back. He has not fully stood. He should return to sitting, recite tashahhud, and complete the prayer. According to Al-Hidayah, he does not need sujud al-sahw; according to Al-Nihayah, he does.
The worshipper should follow the view he deems strongest or a reliable mufti.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود السهو
ومَن سها عن القعدة الأولى، ثم تذكر وهو إلى حال القعود أقرب :
عاد، فجلس، وتشهد .
وإن كان إلى حال القيام أقرب : لم يعد، ويسجد للسهو .
قوله: (ومن سها عن القعدة الأولى، ثم ذَكَرَ وهو إلى حال القعود
أقرب) ، يعني بأن لم يرفع ركبتيه من الأرض.
وفي «المبسوط»): ما لم يستتم قائماً: يعود، وإن استتم: لا يعود،
وصحح
هذا صاحب «الحواشي».
* قوله: (عاد، فقعد، وتشهد)؛ لأن ما قرب إلى الشيء: يأخذ حكمه، كفناء المصر : يأخذ حكم المصر في حق صلاة العيد، والجمعة.
ولم يذكر الشيخ رحمه الله سجود السهو ههنا.

Chapter of Prostration for Forgetfulness. Whoever forgets the first sitting, then remembers while he is closer to the state of sitting: he returns, sits, and recites the tashahhud. And if he is closer to the state of standing: he does not return, and prostrates for forgetfulness. His saying: (Whoever forgets the first sitting, then remembers while he is closer to the state of sitting) means when he has not lifted his knees from the ground. And in Al-Mabsut: as long as he has not fully stood upright, he returns; if he has fully stood, he does not return, and the author of Al-Hawashi corrected this. His saying: (he returns, sits, and recites tashahhud) because what is near to a thing takes its ruling, like the periphery of a city takes the ruling of the city regarding Eid and Friday prayers. The Shaykh (rahimahullah) did not mention prostration for forgetfulness here. And in Al-Hidayah: the most correct is that he does not prostrate, as if he did not stand. And in Al-Nihayah: the chosen view is that he prostrates. And it was found in the handwriting of Al-Makki (rahimahullah): the correct view is that he prostrates. His saying: (And if he is closer to the state of standing, he does not return) because he is like one standing in meaning. (And prostrates for forgetfulness) because he left an obligatory act. If he were to return here, his prayer would be invalidated, just as if he returned after fully standing, because standing is an integral (fard) and the first sitting is an obligatory (wajib), so the fard is not left for the wajib.
Source pages p. 468

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah is a commentary on Al-Quduri's ruling regarding forgetting the first sitting (qa'dah ula) in prayer. The matn states: if one forgets the first sitting and remembers while he is closer to the sitting position (defined as not having lifted his knees from the ground), he should return, sit, and recite the tashahhud. If he is closer to standing, he should not return and should perform two prostrations for forgetfulness (sujud al-sahw). The commentator expands by citing Al-Mabsut, which specifies the threshold as fully standing upright. He then explains the rationale: what is near to something takes its ruling, analogous to the periphery of a city taking the ruling of the city for Eid and Jumu'ah prayers. The commentator notes that Al-Quduri did not mention sujud al-sahw in this case, leading to an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. Al-Hidayah holds the most correct view is no sujud; Al-Nihayah chooses sujud; and Al-Makki also says sujud. The commentator then clarifies that if one were to return after having become more inclined to standing, the prayer becomes invalid, because standing (qiyam) is fard and the first sitting is wajib; one cannot abandon a fard for a wajib.

Key Terms
القعدة الأولى (al-qa'dah al-ula): The first sitting after the second rak'ah in a prayer of three or four rak'ahs, during which the tashahhud is recited.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer, specifically for leaving a wajib or delaying a fard.
قيام (qiyam): Standing in prayer, which is a fard (integral pillar) in the obligatory prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a person forgets the first sitting and remembers after he has fully stood upright, what should he do?
A) Return to the sitting and continue.
B) Do not return and perform sujud al-sahw.
C) Continue the prayer without any additional action.
D) Repeat the prayer from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
The ruling for forgetting the first sitting hinges on proximity: return if near sitting, continue with sujud al-sahw if near standing; and the need for sujud when returning near is disputed among Hanafi authorities.

Forgetting the Final Sitting and Standing for a Fifth Rak'ah
States a sahw ruling and defends it with athar of sujud al-tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for returning to the final sitting when standing for an extra rak'ah, and explain the Hanafi proof using the precedent of sujud al-tilawah.

Core Idea
Return to the final sitting before prostrating in the extra rak'ah — the fifth is void, and athar overrides qiyas.

Forgetting the final sitting (qa'dah akhir) and unintentionally standing for an extra rak'ah is a common sahw scenario in prayer. The Hanafi school provides a precise rule: one must return to sitting as long as the extra rak'ah's prostration has not been performed. This ruling is defended by appealing to the practice of the Prophet and Companions in sujud al-tilawah, demonstrating that an authentic practice (athar) can override strict analogy (qiyas).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is forgetting the final sitting and standing for a fifth rak'ah (in a 4-rak'ah fard prayer). The ruling: one must return to the final sitting if he has not yet prostrated in the fifth rak'ah, and the fifth rak'ah is cancelled (void).
The condition 'before prostrating in the fifth' is critical.
2
Recognize the objection based on qiyas
An objector raises a parallel case: in sujud al-tilawah, one leaves the standing (a fard) for prostration (a wajib). By analogy, leaving a fard for a wajib is problematic. The objection is that similar reasoning would forbid returning to the final sitting because you are leaving the extra standing (is it fard? Actually the extra standing is not fard, but the objector focuses on the principle of leaving a fard for a wajib).
The objection is based on pure qiyas without the athar.
3
Understand the Hanafi response: athar overrides qiyas
The Hanafi response acknowledges that qiyas would indeed forbid leaving the standing, but the athar (the established practice of the Prophet and Companions) overrides it. The Prophet and his Companions used to prostrate for tilawah and leave the standing. This provides direct precedent for the sujud al-tilawah case, and by extension (through the shared 'illa of opposing the disbelievers and showing humility), it justifies returning to the final sitting.
Note the 'illa: the purpose is to show humility and oppose the disbelievers, which is stronger than the general principle of not leaving a fard.
4
Apply the ruling to nafl prayer
The passage adds a note from Al-Wajiz: in nafl prayer, if one forgets the sitting and stands for a third rak'ah (instead of the second sitting), he returns even if fully standing, as long as he has not performed a prostration. This extends the same principle.
In nafl, the third rak'ah is analogous to the fifth in fard; the rule is slightly more lenient (return even after fully standing).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن سها عن القعدة الأخيرة، فقام إلى الخامسة : رجع إلى القعدة مـا لم يسجد في الخامسة، وألغى الخامسة،
فإن قيل : يُشكل على هذا بما إذا تلا آية سجدة، فإنه يترك القيام، وهو
فرض، ويسجد للتلاوة، وهي واجبة، فقد تَرَكَ الفرض لأجل الواجب. قيل: كان القياس هناك أيضاً أن لا يُترك القيام، إلا أنه تُرِكَ القياس بالأثر، «فإنه عليه الصلاة والسلام وأصحابه كانوا يسجدون، ويتركون القيام؛ لأجلها» (١).
والمعنى فيه: أن المقصود من سجدة التلاوة: إظهار التواضع، ومخالفة الكفار، فإنهم كانوا يستكبرون عن السجود، فجُوز ترك القيام؛ تحقيقاً لمخالفتهم.
- وهذا في صلاة الفرض أما في النفل : إذا قام إلى الثالثة من غير قعدة: فإنه يعود ولو استتم قائماً ما لم يقيدها بسجدة. كذا في «الوجيز». * قوله: (وإن سها عن القعدة الأخيرة فقام إلى الخامسة: رجع إلى القعدة ما لم يسجد وألغى الخامسة : أي تركها؛ لأن في رجوعه إلى
And whoever forgets the final sitting, and stands for the fifth [rak'ah]: he returns to the sitting as long as he has not prostrated in the fifth, and he cancels the fifth. If it is objected: there is a problem with this regarding the case of reciting a verse of prostration (sajdah), for in that case he leaves the standing, which is fard, and prostrates for the recitation, which is wajib, thus he leaves the fard for the wajib. It is said: the qiyas there also would be that one should not leave the standing, but the qiyas was left on account of the athar, 'Indeed the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his Companions used to prostrate and leave the standing for its sake.' And the meaning in it is that the purpose of the prostration of recitation is to show humility and to oppose the disbelievers, for they used to be arrogant about prostrating. So leaving the standing was permitted to achieve opposition to them. And this applies to fard prayer. As for nafl prayer: if one stands for the third [rak'ah] without sitting, he returns even if he has fully stood, as long as he has not bound it with a prostration. Thus in Al-Wajiz. His saying: (Whoever forgets the final sitting and stands to the fifth: he returns to the sitting as long as he has not prostrated and cancels the fifth) meaning he leaves it because in his returning to [?].
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah explains the ruling for forgetting the final sitting (qa'dah akhir) in a fard prayer. The matn states: if one forgets the final sitting and stands for a fifth rak'ah, he must return to the sitting as long as he has not prostrated in the fifth rak'ah, and the fifth rak'ah is considered void. The commentator then addresses an objection: how can it be allowed to leave the standing (fard) to return to the final sitting (also fard? Actually, the final sitting is fard, but the standing for the fifth is an extra action, so the objection is about the principle. The objection analogizes to sujud al-tilawah where one leaves standing (fard) for prostration (wajib). The answer is that even there, qiyas would forbid it, but the athar (practice of the Prophet and Companions) overrides the qiyas. The purpose of sujud al-tilawah is to show humility and oppose the disbelievers. Therefore, leaving the standing is permitted. The commentator then adds a note from Al-Wajiz that in nafl prayer, if one stands for the third rak'ah without sitting, he may return even after fully standing, as long as he has not performed a prostration. The passage ends with the commentator's explanation of the matn phrase.

Key Terms
القعدة الأخيرة (al-qa'dah al-akhirah): The final sitting in prayer, after the last rak'ah, during which the tashahhud and salawat are recited. It is a fard (integral) in Hanafi school.
الخامسة (al-khamisah): The fifth rak'ah, which is an extra rak'ah mistakenly performed when one intended to pray four rak'ahs.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of sajdah in the Quran. In Hanafi, it is wajib in prayer and sunnah outside prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Immediately upon remembering, even if he has already prostrated.
B) Only if he has not yet prostrated in the fifth rak'ah.
C) Only if he has not fully stood upright.
D) He should not return; instead, he should complete the fifth rak'ah and then perform sujud al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
When forgetting the final sitting, one must return before prostrating in the extra rak'ah; this ruling is based on athar overriding qiyas, similar to sujud al-tilawah.

Forgetting the Last Sitting and the Fifth Rak'ah: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Sharh expanding on ruling of forgetting last sitting and fifth rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a person forgets the last sitting and stands for a fifth rak'ah, explain the condition of prostration, and distinguish between the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding invalidity.

Core Idea
If you forget the last sitting and stand for a fifth rak'ah, return to sitting before prostrating, or the prayer becomes invalid.

This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayirah addresses a common scenario in prayer: what if you forget the final tashahhud and stand up for an extra rak'ah? The Hanafi school provides a detailed ruling that hinges on whether you have prostrated in the extra rak'ah. The issue also triggers an important intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the point of invalidity and whether the prayer can transform into nafl. Understanding this ruling is crucial for correct practice and for appreciating the nuanced legal reasoning within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the basic rule: if one forgets the last sitting and stands for a fifth rak'ah, he must return to the sitting as long as he has not prostrated in the fifth. He cancels the extra rak'ah and performs sajdah al-sahw.
2
Understand the condition
The key condition is whether the fifth rak'ah has been 'tied' with a prostration (sajdah). If no prostration, the extra standing can be abandoned and the prayer corrected. If prostration occurs, the prayer becomes invalid or transforms.
3
Analyze the objection and response
Consider the objection: leaving fard (standing) for wajib (tilawah prostration) is allowed by sunna, so why not leave fard (sitting) for a wajib? The response explains that tilawah prostration has a distinct purpose (opposing disbelievers) supported by direct evidence, overriding analogy. This clarifies the difference.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Compare the views: Abu Yusuf says invalidity occurs upon placing the forehead; Muhammad says upon raising. Also, Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold the prayer transforms into nafl; Muhammad ibn al-Hasan holds it becomes absolutely invalid. Understand the reasoning behind each.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The text states 'al-mukhtar qawl Muhammad' – the chosen view is Muhammad's. Thus, the prayer is absolutely invalid (batil) upon raising from the prostration in the fifth rak'ah. No transformation to nafl.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود السهو

ومن سها عن القعدة الأخيرة، فقام إلى الخامسة : رجع إلى القعدة ما لم يسجد في الخامسة، وألغى الخامسة، ويسجد للسهو.

فإن قيل : يُشكل على هذا بما إذا تلا آية سجدة، فإنه يترك القيام، وهو فرض، ويسجد للتلاوة، وهي واجبة، فقد تَرَكَ الفرض لأجل الواجب. قيل: كان القياس هناك أيضاً أن لا يُترك القيام، إلا أنه تُرِكَ القياس بالأثر، «فإنه عليه الصلاة والسلام وأصحابه كانوا يسجدون، ويتركون القيام؛ لأجلها». والمعنى فيه: أن المقصود من سجدة التلاوة: إظهار التواضع، ومخالفة الكفار، فإنهم كانوا يستكبرون عن السجود، فجُوز ترك القيام؛ تحقيقاً لمخالفتهم.

وهذا في صلاة الفرض أما في النفل : إذا قام إلى الثالثة من غير قعدة: فإنه يعود ولو استتم قائماً ما لم يقيدها بسجدة. كذا في «الوجيز».

قوله: (وإن سها عن القعدة الأخيرة فقام إلى الخامسة: رجع إلى القعدة ما لم يسجد وألغى الخامسة : أي تركها؛ لأن في رجوعه إلى القعدة: إصلاح صلاته، وذلك ممكن ما لم يسجد؛ لأن ما دون الركعة: محل للرفض. قوله: (ويسجد للسهو)؛ لأنه أخر واجباً، وهو القعدة. قوله: (وإن قيد الخامسة بسجدة: بطل فرضه). يبطل بوضع الجبهة : عند أبي يوسف؛ لأنه سجود كامل. وعند محمد برفعها ؛ لأن تمام الشيء بآخره، وهو الرفع. وفائدته فيما إذا سبقه الحدث في السجود، فرفع رأسه ليتوضأ : فإنه يجوز له البناء عند محمد ؛ لأنه لم يؤد جزءاً من الصلاة مع الحدث، وعند أبي يوسف: لا يجوز له البناء؛ لأنه قد حصل جزء من الصلاة مع الحدث، وهو السجود، فلا يجوز له البناء و المختار: قول محمد. قوله: (وتحولت صلاته نفلاً)، هذا عندهما. وقال محمد: لا تتحول نفلاً، بل تبطل قطعاً؛ لأن الفريضة إذا فسدت بطلت التحريمة، وإذا بطلت عنده: لا يُضم إليها أخرى. قال: لأنها لو لم تبطل تصير تطوعاً و تَرْكُ القعدة على رأس الركعتين في التطوع : مفسد عنده. وأما عندهما فترك القعدة على رأس الركعتين في التطوع: لا يُفسد، فبقيت التحريمة فيضيف إليها أخرى، حتى يصير متنفلاً بست.
Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness

Whoever forgets the last sitting and stands up to the fifth: he returns to the sitting as long as he has not prostrated in the fifth, and he cancels the fifth, and he prostrates for forgetfulness.

If it is said: This is problematic in light of when one recites a verse of prostration, for he leaves the standing, which is obligatory (fard), and prostrates for recitation, which is obligatory (wajib), so he left the fard for the sake of the wajib. It is said: The analogy there also was that one should not leave the standing, but the analogy was abandoned due to the established sunna (athar), “For the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions used to prostrate and leave the standing for its sake.” And the meaning in it is that the purpose of the prostration of recitation is to show humility and to oppose the disbelievers, for they used to refuse to prostrate out of pride, so leaving the standing was permitted to achieve opposition to them.

And this is in the obligatory prayer. As for the supererogatory prayer: if one stands for the third without sitting, he returns even if he has fully stood as long as he has not tied it with a prostration. Thus in al-Wajiz.

His statement: (And whoever forgets the last sitting and stands to the fifth: he returns to the sitting as long as he has not prostrated and cancels the fifth) i.e., leaves it; because in his return to the sitting is the correction of his prayer, and that is possible as long as he has not prostrated, because what is less than a rak'ah is a place for rejection. His statement: (And he prostrates for forgetfulness) because he delayed an obligatory (wajib) element, which is the sitting. His statement: (And if he ties the fifth with a prostration: his obligatory prayer becomes invalid). It becomes invalid by placing the forehead according to Abu Yusuf; because it is a complete prostration. According to Muhammad, it becomes invalid by raising the forehead; because the completion of a thing is by its last part, which is the raising. The benefit of this difference is in the case when he is overtaken by an event (hadath) during the prostration and then raises his head to perform wudu: according to Muhammad, he may build upon his prayer because he did not perform a part of the prayer while in a state of hadath; according to Abu Yusuf, he may not build upon his prayer because he has performed a part of the prayer while in a state of hadath, i.e., the prostration, so he may not build upon his prayer. And the chosen view is the statement of Muhammad. His statement: (And his prayer transforms into supererogatory) this is according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Muhammad said: It does not transform into supererogatory, but rather becomes absolutely invalid; because when the obligatory prayer becomes corrupt, the tahrima (beginning sacredness) is nullified, and according to him, when it is nullified, another cannot be appended to it. He said: Because if it were not nullified, it would become supererogatory, and omitting the sitting at the end of two rak'ats in supererogatory prayer is invalidating according to him. As for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), omitting the sitting at the end of two rak'ats in supererogatory prayer does not invalidate, so the tahrima remains, and he appends another to it, until he becomes a performer of six rak'ats of supererogatory prayer.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) of the ruling on forgetting the last sitting (qa'dah akhirah) in prayer. The commentator begins by stating the ruling: if one forgets the last sitting and stands for a fifth rak'ah, he must return to the sitting as long as he has not prostrated in the fifth rak'ah. He cancels the extra rak'ah and performs the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw) due to delaying the wajib act of sitting.

The text then addresses an objection: why is it permissible to leave the standing (a fard) for the sake of reciting a prostration verse (a wajib), based on the sunna, whereas in the case of the fifth rak'ah, leaving the standing (for the fifth) is not permitted? The answer is that the prostration of recitation is a separate act with a distinct purpose—to show humility and oppose the disbelievers—so the sunna overrides the general analogy. This is supported by the practice of the Prophet and his companions.

Next, the commentator distinguishes between fard and nafl prayers: if in nafl prayer one stands up for a third rak'ah without sitting for the second, he may return as long as he has not prostrated, even if he fully stands.

The commentary then explains each part of the base text: the return to sitting is possible because what is less than a full rak'ah (i.e., the standing before prostrating in the fifth) can be abandoned. The prostration of forgetfulness is required because the last sitting is wajib. When the fifth rak'ah is tied with a prostration (i.e., the sajda is performed), the prayer becomes invalid (for fard) or transforms into nafl according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani; but according to Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, it becomes absolutely invalid. The dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad also extends to the point of nullification: Abu Yusuf says nullification occurs by placing the forehead on the ground, while Muhammad says it occurs by raising it. The practical difference is in the case of a hadath (ritual impurity) during prostration. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Muhammad.

Finally, the text discusses the nature of the prayer: if it transforms into nafl, the tahrima remains and additional rak'ats can be added; but Muhammad argues that if the fard is corrupt, the tahrima is nullified and cannot be appended, and omitting the sitting after two rak'ats in nafl is invalidating to him, whereas his two companions hold that it is not invalidating.

Key Terms
القعدة الأخيرة (al-qa'dah al-akhirah): The last sitting after completing the final rak'ah in prayer, which is wajib in the Hanafi school.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness or omission of a wajib element in prayer.
التحريمة (al-tahrima): The initial takbir that commences the prayer, marking the state of sacredness (hurma) that prohibits worldly actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view within the Hanafi school, if a person forgets the last sitting and stands for a fifth rak'ah, when does his prayer become invalid?
A) Upon standing upright in the fifth rak'ah
B) Upon placing the forehead on the ground for prostration in the fifth rak'ah
C) Upon raising the head from prostration in the fifth rak'ah
D) Only after completing the fifth rak'ah

Key Takeaway
If a person forgets the last sitting and prostrates in a fifth rak'ah, the prayer becomes absolutely invalid according to the relied-upon Hanafi view; the prayer does not become nafl.

The Consequence of Adding a Fifth Rak'ah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ziyadat rak'ah and its consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to EXPLAIN the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding adding a fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'ah fard prayer and STATE the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) and its practical consequences.

Core Idea
When a fifth rak'ah is added to a fard prayer, the Hanafi school does not simply invalidate it; it becomes nafl, requiring a sixth to complete, according to the Sahibayn.

In this lesson, we examine a fascinating intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens if a person mistakenly adds a fifth rak'ah to a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer? Does it become absolutely invalid, or can it be salvaged as a nafl prayer? The answer reveals key principles about the nature of tahrimah, the effect of corruption on the prayer's identity, and the distinction between fard and nafl. We will trace the arguments of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) versus Imam Muhammad himself, and understand which view is relied upon in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Triggering Event
What exactly constitutes adding a fifth rak'ah? The text specifies 'tying it with a prostration' meaning completing the sajdah. Until that point, the extra rak'ah can be abandoned.
The prostration is considered complete according to Abu Yusuf by placing the forehead, and according to Muhammad by raising the head.
2
Understand the Sahibayn's Position
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the fard becomes invalid (batil) but transforms into nafl. Why? Because the tahrimah (sanctification) remains, and they hold that leaving the qad'ah (first sitting) in nafl does not invalidate the prayer.
Therefore the worshipper can add another rak'ah to make the nafl even.
3
Understand Muhammad's Counter-Position
Imam Muhammad argues the fard becomes absolutely invalid (batil qat'an) because corruption voids the tahrimah. Even if it became nafl, leaving the qad'ah would invalidate it according to him.
Thus no addition is possible; the prayer is simply void.
4
Examine the Subsidiary Dispute on Prostration Completion
Within the Sahibayn's own position, there is a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on when the fifth rak'ah is considered tied (by placing forehead vs. raising head). This affects whether one can build upon the prayer after a hadath.
The chosen (mukhtar) is Muhammad's view that the prostration is complete only upon raising the head.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi and Its Consequences
The relied-upon view is that of the Sahibayn: add a sixth rak'ah. Exceptions: Asr and Fajr (no addition due to dislike of nafl). Followers must pray six rak'ahs. No sujud al-sahw required.
The fard obligation must be repeated later.

Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness. And he prostrates for forgetfulness. If he ties the fifth [rak'ah] with a prostration: his obligatory prayer becomes invalid, and his prayer becomes voluntary. The sitting: correction of his prayer, and that is possible as long as he has not prostrated; because what is less than a rak'ah is a place for rejection. * His statement: (And he prostrates for forgetfulness); because he delayed an obligatory [act], which is the sitting. His statement: (If he ties the fifth with a prostration: his obligatory prayer becomes invalid). It becomes invalid by placing the forehead: according to Abu Yusuf; because it is a complete prostration. And according to Muhammad, by raising it; because the completion of a thing is by its end, which is raising. Its benefit is in the case where he is overtaken by an event during prostration, so he raises his head to perform ablution: then it is permissible for him to build upon [the prayer] according to Muhammad; because he did not perform any part of the prayer with the event. According to Abu Yusuf: it is not permissible for him to build; because a part of the prayer occurred with the event, which is the prostration, so it is not permissible for him to build. And the chosen is the saying of Muhammad. His statement: (And his prayer becomes voluntary), this is according to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. And Muhammad said: It does not become voluntary, but rather it becomes absolutely invalid; because when the obligatory prayer becomes corrupt, the sanctification becomes invalid, and when it becomes invalid according to him, no other [rak'ah] is joined to it. He said: because if it did not become invalid, it would become supererogatory, and leaving the sitting at the end of two rak'ahs in supererogatory prayer is invalidating according to him. As for according to them, leaving the sitting at the end of two rak'ahs in supererogatory prayer does not invalidate, so the sanctification remains, and he joins another to it until he becomes a supererogatory worshipper with six. And it was upon him to join a sixth rak'ah to it. His statement: (And it was upon him to join a sixth rak'ah to it). It indicates obligation. And in Al-Mabsut: He said: And it is more beloved to me that he makes the fifth even; because supererogatory prayer is established as pairs, not odd. And this is in all prayers except for Asr, for he does not join to it; because it would be supererogatory before Maghrib, and that is disliked. And in Qadikhan: Except for Fajr, for he does not join to it; because supererogatory prayer before it and after it is disliked. If a person follows him in these two rak'ahs, I mean the fifth and sixth: six rak'ahs become obligatory upon him according to them; because all become supererogatory. According to Muhammad: nothing is obligatory upon him; because the sanctification was cut off when the obligatory prayer became corrupt. And if he does not join a sixth rak'ah: nothing is upon him; because it is conjectural, and the conjectural is not guaranteed, but joining is better. Then when he joins: does he prostrate for forgetfulness according to them? The most correct: Al-Tamartashi: No, he does not prostrate; because the deficiency due to corruption is not compensated by prostration. Thus mentioned he, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage deals with the intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of adding a fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer. The author begins with the chapter on Sujud al-Sahw, stating the basic ruling that one prostrates for forgetfulness when a wajib is delayed. Then he addresses the scenario where a person foolishly adds a fifth rak'ah by performing a prostration (i.e., completing a full rak'ah). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), the obligatory prayer becomes invalid (batil) and transforms into a nafl (supererogatory) prayer. There is a subsidiary disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on when the prostration is considered complete: Abu Yusuf says by placing the forehead, Muhammad says by raising the head. The practical consequence is in the case of a hadath (e.g., breaking wudu) during the prostration. Abu Yusuf would not allow building upon the prayer because a part was performed with the hadath, while Muhammad allows building. The preferred view (mukhtar) is Muhammad's. Then the text discusses Muhammad's own view that the prayer does not become nafl but is absolutely invalid (batil qat'an). His reasoning: when the fard is corrupted, the tahrimah (initial takbir) is void, so nothing can be added. If it were to become nafl, leaving the tashahhud (qad'ah) at the end of two rak'ahs in nafl would invalidate it according to Muhammad. However, according to the Sahibayn, leaving the sitting in nafl does not invalidate, so the tahrimah remains and one can add another rak'ah to make it a six-rak'ah nafl. The text then mentions that it is obligatory (wajib) to add a sixth rak'ah according to the Sahibayn, but Imam Muhammad in Al-Mabsut prefers making it even (shaf') since nafl is prayed in pairs. Exceptions: Asr prayer (because nafl before Maghrib is disliked) and Fajr prayer (because nafl before and after is disliked). If someone follows the imam in these extra rak'ahs, the follower must pray six rak'ahs according to the Sahibayn; according to Muhammad, nothing is required because the imam's tahrimah was cut off. If one does not add a sixth rak'ah, there is no penalty because it is conjectural (maznun), but adding is better. Finally, if one does add the sixth rak'ah, no sujud al-sahw is required because the deficiency arose from corruption, not forgetfulness that can be compensated by prostration. This is the relied-upon view as mentioned by Al-Tamartashi.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness, performed to compensate for a deficiency or delay in the prayer due to forgetfulness.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The initial takbir (Allahu Akbar) that sanctifies the prayer and marks the beginning of the state of ihram in salah.
القعدة (al-qa'dah): The sitting after two rak'ahs in a prayer of more than two rak'ahs (tashahhud).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, if a person adds a fifth rak'ah with a prostration in a four-rak'ah fard prayer, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer becomes absolutely invalid and must be repeated from the beginning.
B) The prayer becomes nafl and must be completed with a sixth rak'ah.
C) The prayer remains valid as fard and the extra rak'ah is ignored.
D) The person must stop immediately and perform sujud al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
When a fifth rak'ah is added to a four-rak'ah fard prayer, the Hanafi school's mufta bihi is that it becomes a nafl prayer, which must be completed with a sixth rak'ah; the fard obligation must be repeated later.

Adding a Sixth Rak'ah When Mistakenly Standing for Fifth
States the wajib action when standing for a fifth rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adding a sixth rak'ah when one mistakenly stands for a fifth, and distinguish between the positions of the Sahibayn and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Adding a sixth rak'ah is wajib; if omitted, no penalty because the matter is conjectural.

This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayirah deals with a common mistake in prayer: standing for a fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'ah fard. The author explains the obligation to add a sixth rak'ah, the exceptions for Asr and Fajr, and the intra-Hanafi differences regarding followers. We will walk through the legal reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
When a person mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah, the ruling is that he must add a sixth rak'ah to make the voluntary prayer even (shaf'). This is wajib based on the wording in al-Asl.
The word 'عليه' in the text indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi terminology.
2
Note the exceptions for Asr and Fajr
For Asr prayer, adding a sixth is not done because it would become a voluntary prayer before Maghrib, which is disliked. For Fajr, adding is also not done because voluntary prayer before and after Fajr is disliked.
These exceptions are based on the general dislike of nafl at those times.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute on followers
If a follower joins the imam in the fifth and sixth rak'ahs, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani), the follower must perform six rak'ahs (the original four plus two) because the entire prayer becomes voluntary. According to Muhammad alone, nothing is obligatory because the ihram was broken when the fard became invalid.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the consequence of not adding a sixth
If the person does not add a sixth rak'ah, there is no penalty because the matter is conjectural (maznun), and conjectural matters do not incur legal liability. However, adding is still preferable (afdal).
The principle: al-maznun ghayr madmun (the conjectural is not guaranteed).
5
Determine when sajdat al-sahw is performed
After adding the sixth rak'ah and completing the prayer, the person does not perform sajdat al-sahw according to the correct view (al-sahih), because the deficiency was due to invalidity of the original fard, not a forgetfulness within a valid prayer. However, if the error was merely omitting salam, then sajdat al-sahw is performed.
This is based on istihsan (juristic preference) overriding qiyas.
